---
id : <TEXT>AlmondCrunchCereal</TEXT>
categories : [ "cookiesandbars" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 225°F. In a very large bowl, combine oats, coconut, wheat germ, sunflower seeds, and sesame seeds.</p>
<p>In a separate bowl, combine honey and oil; mix well.</p>
<p>Add honey to dry ingredients, a little at a time, stirring until well-mixed.</p>
<p>Add cold water, a little at a time, until mixture is crumbly.</p>
<p>Spread mixture in a lightly oiled, large heavy baking sheet.  Spread mixture evenly. Bake for 1½ hours, stirring every 15 minutes.</p>
<p>Add almonds and bake for 30 minutes more, until thoroughly dry and light brown.</p>
<p>Turn off oven and let cereal cool in oven. Add raisins if desired.</p>
<p>Store tightly covered.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>3</td><td>cups</td><td>rolled oats, uncooked</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>dried coconut, shredded</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>wheat germ</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>sunflower seeds, raw</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sesame seeds</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>honey</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sunflower oil</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>cold water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>slivered almonds</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>raisins, optional</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "grains", "nuts" ]
title : <TEXT>Almond Crunch Cereal</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You can use a light sesame oil or another oil instead of the sunflower oil. Just try to get something that has a little flavor (but not olive)!</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Rodale Cookbook</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I've never eaten this cereal for breakfast. Instead, I've made “Hi-Energy Bars” with it, or just eaten it out of hand as a snack.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>AltonBrownstheChewy</TEXT>
categories : [ "cookiesandbars" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 375°F and place racks in the top third and bottom third of oven.</p>
<p>Melt the butter in a 2-quart saucepan. Let cool. Sift together flour, salt and baking soda. Pour the butter into mixer. Add the sugar and brown sugar and beat with paddle. Whisk together the egg, yolk, milk and vanilla. Reduce mixer speed and slowly add egg mixture. Gradually integrate the dry ingredients, stopping to scrape the bowl. Add chocolate chips slowly. Chill the dough for 1 hour.</p>
<p>Scoop the dough into 1½ ounce portions onto a parchment-lined half sheet, 6 cookies per pan.</p>
<p>Bake 2 pans at a time for 15 minutes, rotating pan halfway through. </p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>sticks</td><td>unsalted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>2 ¼</td><td>cup</td><td>bread flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>kosher salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>baking soda</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>cup</td><td>brown sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td></td><td>egg</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td></td><td>egg yolk</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>whole milk</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>semisweet chocolate chips</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Alton Brown’s “the Chewy”</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>0</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Kim and Dana Woodward: Gourmet Goodness from Our Kitchen to Yours!</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>From Kim and Dana: Christine Young-Sikes made these for Dana … now we all have to make these for Dana … and no one can really live up to Christine when it comes to baking “the chewy!”</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>AnnesDillyBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Dissolve yeast in water. Add cottage cheese. Add remaining ingredients, using enough flour to make a stiff dough. Beat well. Brush top with oil or margarine.</p>
<p>Cover and set in a warm place to rise.</p>
<p>When doubled, about an hour, beat the dough down with a spoon and place in a well-greased loaf pan.</p>
<p>Butter top and bake in a preheated 325°F oven for 25 minutes.</p>
<p>Increase heat to 350°Fand bake until well-browned, about 15-20 minutes.</p>
<p>Cool on rack.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>warm water, (105 - 115°)</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>low-fat cottage cheese, warmed</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>margarine, melted and cooled</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dill weed</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>baking soda</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg</td></tr> <tr><td>2 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>flour, sifted</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Anne's Dilly Bread</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>The original recipe called for 1 tablespoon dill seed, but I like the dill weed better. Fresh dill is great, but you need a lot (3 to 4 tablespoons chopped). </p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Herbcraft</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This bread is superb toasted and spread with some strawberry preserves.  I've probably made this bread recipe more than any other.</p>
<p>I have used white flour, whole wheat flour, and a mixture of flours for this recipe. They all work.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>1 loaf</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ApplePiewithaTwist</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Crust: In a medium bowl, whisk together the flour and salt. Add the shortening, mixing till well combined. Cut the butter into small cubes or pats, and work it into the dry ingredients (using your fingers, a pastry blender or fork, or a mixer) until the dough is unevenly crumbly.</p>
<p>Sprinkle in the ice water, continuing to mix until the dough is cohesive. Grab a handful; if it holds together willingly, and doesn't seem at all dry or crumbly, you've added enough liquid.</p>
<p>Divide the dough roughly in half, with one half slightly larger than the other. If you have a scale, the pieces will weigh about 11 ounces and 9 ounces. Shape each piece of dough into a disk. Roll the edges along a floured work surface (as though the disk were a wheel), in order to smooth them out.  Pat each disk till it's about 1" thick, wrap in plastic wrap, and refrigerate for a minimum of 30 minutes. You may also chill the dough overnight, or for up to 3 days.</p>
<p>Remove the dough from the refrigerator. If it's been chilled longer than 30 minutes, allow it to warm a bit and become flexible, about 15 to 30 minutes. While the dough is warming, prepare the filling, and preheat the oven to 350°F.</p>
<p>Filling: Place the sliced apples in a medium mixing bowl, and stir in the sugar, boiled cider, spices, salt, vanilla, and lemon juice. As you stir, the mixture will become syrupy. Add the butter and flour, and stir until everything is well blended. Set it aside.</p>
<p>Flour your work surface, and roll the larger piece of the dough into a 14" circle. Transfer the dough to a 9" regular (not deep-dish) pie pan that's at least 1 1/4" deep. Spoon the filling into the crust.</p>
<p>Roll the top crust about into an 11" circle, and place it over the filling.  Fold the edge of the bottom crust up over the edge of the top crust, squeeze them together, and crimp nicely. Cut a decorative slit (or a quarter-sized hole) in the center of the crust, for steam to escape.</p>
<p>Place the pie pan on a cookie sheet (to catch any spills), and bake the pie for 45 minutes.</p>
<p>Gently place a sheet of aluminum foil atop the pie, covering its entire surface, and continue to bake for an additional 1 hour, 15 minutes, for a total of 2 hours, till the top crust is golden brown and the filling is bubbly.</p>
<p>Remove the pie from the oven, and allow it to cool overnight, for best texture. If you cut into it too soon, the filling will be watery, and will ooze out.</p>
<p>To serve warm, heat individual slices briefly in the microwave. Serve with vanilla ice cream, if desired.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Crust</td></tr> <tr><td>2 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>vegetable shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>10</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>unsalted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>7</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>ice water, enough to make a cohesive dough</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Filling</td></tr> <tr><td>8</td><td>cups</td><td>apples, peeled and sliced</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>cups</td><td>confectioners' sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>boiled cider</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>nutmeg</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cinnamon</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>allspice</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>fresh lemon juice</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>unsalted butter, melted</td></tr> <tr><td>¼</td><td>cup</td><td>flour</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Apple Pie with a Twist</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You can substitute frozen apple juice concentrate for the boiled cider, if you must.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>10</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>King Arthur Flour</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is a great pie, with a deep apple flavor. And yes, you really do cook it for all that time.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>9-inch pie</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ArizonaCheeseStrata</TEXT>
categories : [ "cheeseandeggs" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F. Lightly butter a 9-inch glass pie plate.</p>
<p>Whisk milk, eggs, salt, and pepper in a medium bowl.</p>
<p>Add cheese, green onion, and jalapeño. Add bread and stir until moistened. Pour into pie plate.</p>
<p>Let stand until bread absorbs most of moisture, about 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Press bread down into mixture a few times to aid absorption.</p>
<p>Bake, uncovered, until light brown and crusty, about 20 minutes.</p>
<p>A knife inserted into the center should come out clean.</p></TEXT>

title : <TEXT>Arizona Cheese Strata</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>AromaticYellowRicePeelayChaaval</TEXT>
categories : [ "riceandgrains" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Wash rice in several changes of water, until most of starch is removed. Drain. Place rice in 5 cups water and let soak for 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Drain in a sieve for at least 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Combine all ingredients except butter in a heavy pot; bring to a boil. Cover with a tight fitting lid and cook for 25 minutes over very, very low heat. Let pot rest undisturbed for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Cut butter in small chunks and add to rice; mix gently with a fork. Remove the cinnamon and cloves before serving.</p></TEXT>

<p>Mix all ingredients and place in a medium casserole dish.</p>
<p>Heat in oven for 20 minutes.</p>
<p>Note: you may store the mixture in the refrigerator for up to 12 hours before heating.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>14</td><td>ounces</td><td>artichoke hearts, drained and chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>mayonnaise</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>Parmesan cheese, grated</td></tr> <tr><td>1/8</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>garlic powder</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "Appetizers" ]
title : <TEXT>Artichoke Dip</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Do not use the marinated artichoke hearts, just get the ones that are canned in water. Be picky: some brands have woody artichokes and you want to avoid these. I think that frozen artichoke hearts, if you can find them, work even better. Thaw them well before using.</p>
<p>Also, low-fat or imitation mayonnaise may not work in this dish - sometimes it will separate into its oil and icky components. Even some full-fat brands work better than others.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>20</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Judy Kelly / Rave Reviews from the Kitchen</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I like this dish way too much, so I never cook it any more. In a sitting, I could consume 100 grams of fat.</p>
<p>I suggest that you test this recipe with your preferred brands before you serve it to guests, because it can make a big difference.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BakedBrieinPuffPastry</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 375°F. Line a baking sheet with parchment paper.</p>
<p>Thaw pastry sheet for 20 minutes at room temperature (or overnight in refrigerator).</p>

id : <TEXT>BakedMacaroniandCheese</TEXT>
categories : [ "pasta" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In large pan, boil macaroni in 3 quarts boiling water and the 1 tablespoon salt.</p>
<p>Melt margarine and add chopped onion, stir in flour, mustard, salt and pepper. Slowly add milk and cook until smooth. Slice about ¾ of the cheese into the sauce and still until melted. Drain the cooked macaroni and place  in a casserole - cover with sauce, tossing lightly with a fork to coat all macaroni.</p>
<p>Grate remaining cheese over the top. Toss bread crumbs with 4 tsp. melted margarine; sprinkle over the cheese.</p>
<p>Bake uncovered at 300°Ffor 20 minutes.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BakedSquash</TEXT>
categories : [ "vegetables", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F. In a 10-inch skillet, melt the butter.</p>
<p>Cook squash and onion until squash is soft and onion is translucent.</p>
<p>If there is a lot of liquid, drain the squash and onion. You want it to be moist and buttery, but not swimming in liquid.</p>
<p>In a medium bowl, combine ½ cup of the cheddar cheese, eggs, sage, and black pepper. Mix in squash and onion. Mix in sour cream if desired. Mix in the bread crumbs. Pour into a greased 8” x 8” casserole dish and sprinkle remaining cheese on top. Top with extra bread crumbs if desired.</p>
<p>Bake about 25 minutes, until firm.</p></TEXT>

tags : [ "Casseroles" ]
title : <TEXT>Baked Squash</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You could use an 8-inch square casserole dish for this recipe, but I prefer a slightly smaller dish so the casserole is a little deeper. </p>

servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Lisa Guinn</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I altered this recipe from the original from the old “Women of Worthen” cookbook, to make it more like the Dixie Cafe's version, which Steve and I both enjoy. But over time, we saw other recipes that we liked, and so I kept tweaking this one. The black pepper really brings out the flavor of the cheese and the squash. You should have about 5-6 cups of sliced squash - you want there to be lots of squash, with the other ingredients just binding the mixture. Ritz crackers are an excellent alternative to the bread crumbs, but they do add calories!</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BananaPudding</TEXT>
categories : [ "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Mix flour, sugar and salt in the top of a double boiler.</p>
<p>Slowly stir in milk and cook until the mixture thickens, stirring. It should coat the back of a spoon, so that the pudding does not run when you draw your finger across the spoon.</p>
<p>Stir a little of the hot mixture into the beaten egg yolks and add the egg yolk mixture to the pot. Cook 2 minutes.</p>
<p>Remove from heat and add vanilla. Add the banana extract if you are using it.</p>
<p>Cool until just warm. Line a pan or oven-proof serving bowl with vanilla wafers. Stir bananas into pudding and pour in pan or serving bowl.</p>
<p>Meringue: In a large clean bowl, beat egg whites until soft peaks form.</p>
<p>Beat in the remaining ¼ cup sugar, 1 tablespoon at a time, until it dissolves completely. Spread meringue over the pudding.</p>
<p>Bake at 350° for 12 to 15 minutes.</p>

introduction : <TEXT><p>Jackson's vanilla wafers are the very best for banana pudding, but I don't think you can find them outside of Arkansas. These ribs are tender and flavorful.  If you must, you can grill the ribs for the last 30 minutes of cooking, over medium-low coals.  Baste the ribs with the sauce often. Or smoke the ribs until almost done (instead of baking them for the first 90 minutes), then finish them with the sauce in the oven.</p>

directions : <TEXT><p>Always start with *cold* water.</p>

introduction : <TEXT><p>I often double this recipe. You may use as little as 1.5 pounds chicken. Make sure that you get pieces with lots of bones (necks, wings, backs) and leave the skin on for the best taste. I think that this stock is so much better than anything you can buy -- you really can taste the difference.  Plus, it has no salt. I use large mouth quart canning jars to store the stock. When I make a bunch of stock, I'll sometimes freeze it. You probably shouldn't keep it in the refrigerator for more than a couple of weeks. </p>

id : <TEXT>BasicPolenta</TEXT>
categories : [ "riceandgrains" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In medium saucepan, bring 4½ cups water and salt to a boil over medium heat. Gradually add cornmeal, stirring almost continuously with a wire whisk.</p>
<p>When mixture starts to thicken, stir in butter with a wooden spoon.</p>
<p>Reduce heat to low.</p>
<p>Continue to stir until polenta is quite thick and creamy, taking care to scrape entire bottom and sides of pan.</p>
<p>This takes about 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Soft polenta: serve at once, use in recipes as directed, or hold over a pan of simmering water for up to 1 hour. Also, you may want to add extra water, by the tablespoonful, during the last 5 to 8 minutes of cooking.</p>
<p>Firm polenta: immediate scrape warm mixture into a lightly oiled 9 x 5-inch loaf pan.  Cool to room temperature, about 30 minutes.  Cover with plastic wrap and refrigerate overnight.</p>
<p>Butter or oil:  You may use olive oil in place of the butter if desired.  Some recipes actually use an entire stick of butter, and 3 to 4 tablespoons is not uncommon.  Extra butter improves the flavor and texture, but it is not necessary.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>yellow cornmeal</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>butter</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Basic Polenta</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Vegetarian Times, March 2000</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This basic polenta recipe has a lot of notes and variations, so you should be able to have polenta any way you want.  Also, this recipe is perfect for making polenta to be used in other recipes.  Be careful when the polenta starts to thicken -- it tends to spatter.  Hot polenta will stick to your skin and burn, so wear an oven mitt and protect your arms with sleeves.</p>
</TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BasicWaffleRecipe</TEXT>
categories : [ "quickbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat the waffle iron.</p>
<p>Sift dry ingredients together into a large mixing bowl. Set aside.</p>
<p>Separate eggs carefully.  Put the whites into a medium mixing bowl, and the yolks into a small mixing bowl.</p>
<p>In a medium mixing bowl, beat egg whites until stiff. Set aside.</p>
<p>In a small mixing bowl, beat egg yolks until thick and lemon-colored.</p>
<p>Beat in milk. Stir mixture into dry ingredients until smooth. Stir in oil.</p>
<p>Carefully fold in egg whites, one third at a time. Do not over-mix; leaving a few little fluffs of egg white is expected.</p>
<p>Bake in a preheated waffle iron.</p>
<p>Waffles are done when little or no steam is escaping.  A standard sized waffle iron will require about 1 cup of batter.</p>
<p>In my Croquade waffle iron: Preheat on setting 5. Cook about 3½ minutes per waffle.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>flour, sifted</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>large</td><td>eggs</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>milk</td></tr> <tr><td>7</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>vegetable oil</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Basic Waffle Recipe</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Since you can only cook one waffle at a time, this recipe will take about an hour.</p>
<p>You will need 3 mixing bowls for this recipe; a small one for the egg yolks, a medium one for the egg whites, and a large one for the batter.You can freeze left-over waffles.</p>
<p>To reheat frozen waffles: First, thaw them for a little bit in the microwave. Then place them in a toaster-oven or regular oven for about 5 minutes to reheat and re-crisp them.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Toastmaster Wafflemaker Manual</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is my go-to recipe for waffles, and has been for decades. It will make a crisp and eggy waffle, just like real American waffles before the Belgian craze hit. (I don’t like Belgian waffles, although I expect you can use this batter to make them.)</p>
</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>Beignets</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Place warm water in a large bowl, then sprinkle yeast on top and stir until dissolved.</p>
<p>Add sugar, eggs and evaporated milk.</p>
<p>Stir in 4 cups of flour and beat with a wooden spoon for 3 minutes.</p>
<p>Beat in the shortening, then add the remaining flour ⅓ cup at a time, beating with a wooden spoon. When dough becomes too stiff to work with the spoon, use your hands. Cover the bowl with plastic wrap and refrigerate overnight.</p>
<p>Roll out the dough on a floured surface to 1/8-inch thickness. Cut into rectangles 2½ x 3½-inches with a sharp knife. Preheat oil to 360°F.</p>
<p>Fry 3 or 4 beignets at a time until puffed and brown on both sides (2 to 3 minutes per batch). Turn them once or twice to brown evenly. Place them on paper towels in a 200°Foven to keep warm.</p>
<p>Sprinkle with confectioner's sugar and serve hot.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>warm water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>pkg</td><td>active dry yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>eggs</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>evaporated whole milk, canned</td></tr> <tr><td>7</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>shortening, melted and cooled</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>oil, for frying</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>confectioner's sugar</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Beignets (New Orleans French Market Doughnuts)</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>The evaporated milk should not be diluted; use it straight from the can.</p>
<p>This recipe makes a big batch of small beignets; a person can easily eat 3 or 4. But you could halve the recipe.  After all, it will take about an hour to cook 5 dozen of these when you can only fry 4 at a time.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>24</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The New Orleans Cookbook</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>When I was much younger, I used to go to New Orleans from time to time. It was almost a requirement that we would have these doughnuts at Cafe du Monde. Unlike most recipes, this one is an almost perfect duplication of the restaurant version.  think that ¼ teaspoon of nutmeg makes it a perfect match.</p>
</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>Biscuits</TEXT>
categories : [ "quickbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 450°F.</p>
<p>Sift dry ingredients together. Cut in shortening.</p>
<p>Add enough milk to make a soft dough that can be handled easily.</p>
<p>Turn onto a lightly floured board. Knead lightly for ½ minute, so dough will stick together. Roll or pat out to between ½ and 1 inch thick. Cut into biscuits with a floured cutter.</p>
<p>Place on a greased baking sheet (or pan). Bake for 12 to 15 minutes, until golden brown.</p>
<p>Buttermilk version:  Same directions, but use</p>
<p>2 cup sifted flour</p>
<p>1 tsp. baking powder</p>
<p>½ tsp. baking soda</p>
<p>¼ cup shortening (do not reduce amount)</p>
<p>⅔ cup sour milk or buttermilk</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>flour, sifted</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>2/3</td><td>cups</td><td>milk</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Biscuits</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>If you are making the sweet milk version, you can cut the shortening down to 2 tablespoons, according to this World War II cookbook. But your biscuits will not be as tender.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Good Housekeeping, 1944</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>If your biscuits aren't as tender as your grandmother's, it could be because you are using a harder flour; using pastry flour, if you can find it, may help.  Or, maybe she used lard - you aren't trying to use some shortening substitute, are you?  But maybe she was just a better biscuit cook.  When I made biscuits a couple of times a week, mine were much better than they are now. Or check out the Tender Biscuits recipe.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BitesizeCheesePuffs</TEXT>
categories : [ "appetizerssnacks" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 375°F.</p>
<p>Boil water in a small pan.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, mix flour, Parmesan, cayenne pepper and nutmeg.</p>
<p>Add butter to boiling water. When butter melts, add flour mixture all at once. Beat well.</p>
<p>Continue beating until the mixture pulls together and leaves the sides of the pan - about 1½ minutes. Cool slightly. Beat in the eggs one at a time. Drop by spoonfuls onto lightly greased baking sheets. (Each will spread slightly.)</p>
<p>Bake for 25 minutes, or until puffed and golden brown.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BlackEyedPeaSoup</TEXT>
categories : [ "beansandpeas", "soups" ]

tags : [ "Beans" ]
title : <TEXT>Black-Eyed Pea Soup</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>If you are using canned black-eyed peas, you might want to drain and rinse them before using. You will have to add some water to compensate, but I hate the liquid that is in the can. I don't like canned blacked-eyed peas, so I usually soak and then cook about 2 cups of dried peas in water and then add them to the recipe. Don't add dried black-eyed peas without precooking them, because they may never get tender in the salty and acidic stock.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Linda Thompson</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This recipe came to us from Linda Thompson, Steve's cousin. It is exactly as she said: "nice and easy and so good."  Of course, we have modified the recipe slightly: the original called for 1 can of plain black-eyed peas and one can of black-eyed peas with jalapeños. It also called for 2 cans of stewed tomatoes or Rotel; using only stewed tomatoes would obviously make the recipe milder. I like to add ham to this recipe, especially since I often cook this for New Year's Day and I often have leftover ham with a bone.</p>
<p>Steve sometimes adds a pound of browned ground beef to the recipe, instead of the ham. Personally, I don't see the need for that, but if you do, you will probably need to adjust the seasonings a bit.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BlueberryMuffins</TEXT>
categories : [ "quickbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>
<p>Line 12 muffin tins with paper liners or coat with non-stick cooking spray.</p>
<p>In a large bowl, cream the butter and sugar with an electric mixer until fluffy. Add the egg and vanilla; beat until fluffy. Blend in the buttermilk.</p>
<p>Sift in the flour, salt and baking powder and mix until almost smooth. Drop blueberries on top and stir until just blended with a spoon, being careful not to break up the blueberries too much.</p>
<p>Spoon about ¼ cup batter into each muffin cup. Bake until golden brown and a skewer inserted in the middle comes out clean, about 17 to 20 minutes. If you used frozen blueberries, add about 3 minutes to the cooking time.</p>
</TEXT>

tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Blueberry Muffins</TEXT>

time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Now that we have blueberry bushes in the back yard, I had to find a good muffin recipe for Steve. This one is great, although it is pretty cake-like. The original recipe had a topping, but that’s even more calories!</p>

id : <TEXT>BraisedShortRibs</TEXT>
categories : [ "beef"]
directions : <TEXT><p>Split meat into individual ribs.</p>
<p>Heat oil in a dutch oven over high heat.</p>
<p>Rub ribs with salt. When pot is hot, add ribs and brown on all sides. Do not crowd ribs; work in batches if necessary.</p>
<p>When all ribs are browned, remove them from the pan and add onions, celery and carrots. Sauté 1 minute to brown lightly.</p>
<p>Stir in tomatoes, garlic, vinegar, Worcestershire sauce, bay leaves and pepper.</p>
<p>Return ribs to pot and turn to coat. Add just enough beef stock to cover ribs.</p>
<p>Bring to a boil and then reduce heat to gently simmering. Cover and cook until very tender, about 2½ hours.</p>
<p>Remove ribs from pot and place in serving dish. Remove as much fat from the stock as possible and reduce it if desired.</p>
<p>Pour stock and vegetables over the top of the ribs; sprinkle with the green onions.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>vegetable oil</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>lbs.</td><td>beef short ribs</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>onion, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>celery, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>carrot, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>tomatoes, peeled, seeded and c</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>garlic, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>red wine vinegar</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>worcestershire sauce</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td></td><td>bay leaves</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>black pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>low fat beef broth, or more if needed</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>green onions, chopped</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Braised Short Ribs</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You may use fresh or canned tomatoes. If you use canned tomatoes, you will not need as much beef stock.</p>
<p>You can easily reduce the fat in this recipe by removing the stock after the ribs are cooked, placing the stock in the refrigerator, then skimming the fat from the surface.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Emeril Lagasse, Food Network</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This recipe is very tasty, and makes a huge amount of stock.  You can serve the ribs with the stock, but you have other choices. One: you can remove the ribs and vegetables with a slotted spoon and make gravy with the stock. Two: You can remove the ribs, and then use a blender to puree the vegetables to make a thicker stock/gravy.</p>
<p>Be sure to serve this with something to soak up the stock: mashed potatoes and bread are good.</p>
<p>By the way, this recipe says "4 servings" not "will serve 4 people." This is a bit more than 2 people can eat (or at least more than they should), but it will not serve 4 adults.</p>
</TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BreakthroughPolenta</TEXT>
categories : [ "riceandgrains" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 350°F. Grease a heavy 12-inch ovenproof saucepan or Dutch oven. Add the cornmeal, stock, oil and salt. Stir with a fork or whisk until well-blended. The mixture will separate, but don’t worry - it won’t come together for more than half the cooking time. Bake uncovered for 1 hour and 20 minutes, or until the polenta is creamy and tender. Stir with a long-pronged fork; adjust the seasoning and bake for 10 minutes more. Remove from the oven and let rest for 5 minutes. Stir in additional butter or grated cheese if desired. Pour onto a wooden pizza peel or into a buttered bowl.</p>
<p>To adjust the thickness, vary the amount of liquid, not the cooking time:</p>
<p>Very soft - use 12 cups liquid</p>
<p>Soft - use 10 cups</p>
<p>Medium - use 8 cups</p>
<p>Very firm - use 6 cups</p>
<p>For most purposes, use soft polenta, but for polenta that is to be sautéed or broiled, make very firm polenta.  Spread it on a platter and let it cool, then cut and sauté or broil.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>cornmeal</td></tr> <tr><td>9</td><td>cups</td><td>chicken stock, or water</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>olive oil, or butter</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt, or more if needed</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Breakthrough Polenta</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>This recipe can be halved, if you like: use an oiled 8-inch saucepan to bake it and cook it only for 45 minutes instead of 1 hour 20 minutes.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The Best American Recipes 1999</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>The breakthrough here is that you don't have to stand over this, stirring, for the entire cooking time.  It won't spit hot cornmeal on you, either.  </p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>BurgeroftheGods</TEXT>
categories : [ "beef"]
directions : <TEXT><p>Trim off any fat from the meat before you cube it.</p>
<p>Put half of the sirloin in the food processor. Pulse for 1 second; do this 10 times.</p>
<p>Take out the chopped meat and put it in a large bowl.</p>
<p>Repeat with the other half of the sirloin.</p>
<p>Put half of the chuck in the food processor. Pulse for 1 second; do this 10 times.</p>
<p>Take out the chopped meat and put it in the bowl.</p>
<p>Repeat with the other half of the chuck.</p>
<p>Add the salt to the meat. Knead gently with your fingers.</p>
<p>Weigh out 5 oz patties with a scale. Shape them about ¾-inch thick and about 4 inches in diameter. Slightly depress the center of each burger.</p>
<p>Heat a griddle to medium-high heat for 2-3 minutes. Cook the patties, without crowding. DO NOT MASH WITH A SPATULA; that is simply evil.</p>
<p>Cook for 4 minutes on each side for medium-rare.</p>
<p>I prefer 5 minutes on each side for medium.</p>
<p>Let rest for 2 minutes, then serve.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>lb.</td><td>beef sirloin, cut in 1½-inch cubes</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>lb.</td><td>beef chuck, cut in 1½-inch cubes</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>kosher salt</td></tr></table></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ButterhornRolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Soften yeast in lukewarm milk; let stand for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Add salt, shortening, sugar and eggs.</p>
<p>Add flour a little at a time until a soft, kneadable dough is formed.</p>
<p>You may need only about 4 cups of flour.</p>
<p>Knead dough until smooth and elastic. Cover and let rise until double.</p>
<p>Punch down and let rise a second time until double.</p>
<p>Roll dough into a circle and cut into 15 wedges; roll up to make crescents and place in well-greased pans.</p>
<p>Let rise until tripled.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 400°F. Bake for 12 to 15 minutes.</p>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>

id : <TEXT>Casserolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Heat milk, honey, 1 tablespoon butter and salt until butter melts and honey dissolves. Place in a medium bowl and let cool to lukewarm.</p>
<p>Melt remaining butter in a separate pan.</p>
<p>Add yeast to milk; stir to dissolve and let stand for 5 minutes, or until yeast begins to foam.</p>
<p>Add flour and beat 50 strokes until batter is smooth and elastic.</p>
<p>Cover bowl and let dough rise for 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Pour half of the melted butter into a 9 x 9-inch baking pan.</p>
<p>Stir the batter to remove air bubbles. Drop by heaping tablespoons into the buttered pan.</p>
<p>Pour remaining butter over the top and let rise until double (15 to 20 minutes more). Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>
<p>Bake for 30 minutes; serve hot.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>milk</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>honey</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>whole wheat flour</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Casserolls</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>One tablespoon yeast is the equivalent of 1 package of yeast. If you buy the quick-acting yeast, the rising time for this recipe will be cut almost in half.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Recipes for a Small Planet</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>These rolls require no kneading or shaping. Compared to most yeast bread recipes, this one is pretty quick. And although there is a lot of fat, or maybe because of it, they taste great.  Just don't expect them to look like regular rolls; mine tend to be a little flatter in general.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>16 rolls</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F. Set the freshly-grated potato in a colander. Salt it and let it sit for 10 minutes, then squeeze out the excess water. id : <TEXT>ChickeninaSweetRedPepperSauce</TEXT>
categories : [ "chicken" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Skin all chicken pieces. If using breasts, divide them into 4 parts.</p>
<p>Place onion, ginger, garlic, almonds, peppers, cumin, coriander, turmeric, cayenne and salt in a blender or food processor; blend to a smooth paste.</p>
<p>Place oil in a large wide skillet over medium-high heat. When hot, avert eyes and add onion paste. Stir and fry for 10 to 12 minutes.</p>
<p>Add chicken, water, lemon juice and pepper. Stir and bring to a boil. Cover, turn heat to low and simmer for 25 minutes, stirring occasionally.</p>
<p>Add up to ½ cup more water if needed. Wait until chicken has simmered a bit before adding more water, as the sauce tends to thin a bit as the it cooks.</p></TEXT>

tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Chicken in a Sweet Red Pepper Sauce (lal Masale Wali Murgh)</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>We usually use chicken thighs for this dish, but you can use any chicken pieces that you like. If you are using boneless chicken, then use about 1½ pounds of chicken. id : <TEXT>ChocolateBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads", "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Lightly grease a 6-inch round and deep cake pan.  (If you prefer, you can bake this bread on a lightly greased baking sheet.)</p>
<p>Sift the flour, cocoa powder and salt in to a large bowl. Stir in the sugar. Make a well in the center.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, mix the yeast with 4 tablespoons of water, then stir in the remaining water. When completely dissolved, add to the center of the flour. Gradually mix to a dough. Knead in the softened butter.</p>
<p>Turn out on a floured surface and knead until smooth and elastic. Place in a lightly oiled bowl. Cover and let rise for about 1 hour or until doubled in bulk.</p>
<p>Turn out onto a lightly floured surface and punch down. Gently knead in the chopped chocolate. Cover with lightly oiled plastic wrap and let rest for 5 minutes. Shape the dough and place in pan. Cover again with the lightly oiled plastic wrap. Let rise in a warm place until doubled, about 45 minutes.</p>
<p>Preheat the oven to 425°F. Bake the bread for 10 minutes, then reduce the temperature to 375°F and bake for another 25 - 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Brush the top with melted butter. Let cool on a wire rack.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>3</td><td>cups</td><td>white bread flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>cocoa powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>ounce</td><td>fresh yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>water, lukewarm</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>butter, softened</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>ounces</td><td>semisweet chocolate, coarsely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>melted butter, for brushing on loaf</td></tr></table></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ChocolateCreamPie</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>In medium saucepan, combine sugar, flour, and salt. Gradually stir in milk. Add chopped chocolate to mixture. Cook and stir over medium heat until bubbly.</p>

id : <TEXT>ChocolateLayerCake</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>The eggs and butter should be at room temperature before you begin.</p>
<p>In a medium bowl, whisk cocoa and boiling water until smooth. Cover with plastic wrap and set aside to cool to room temperature, about 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°Fabout 20 minutes before baking.</p>
<p>Prepare one 9-inch round cake pan (2” deep): coat the bottom with shortening. Insert a round of parchment paper to fit the bottom. Spray with a baking spray that contains flour.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, whisk the eggs, 3 tablespoons of water, and the vanilla until lightly combined.</p>
<p>In the bowl of a stand mixer fitted with the flat beater, mix the flour, sugar, baking powder and salt on low speed for about 30 seconds. Add the butter, oil and cocoa mixture. Mix on low speed until dry ingredients are moistened. Raise the speed to medium and beat for 1 ½ minutes. Scrape down the sides of the bowl.</p>
<p>Starting on medium-low speed, gradually add the egg mixture in two parts. Beat on medium speed for 30 seconds after each part, to incorporate the ingredients and strengthen the structure. Scrape down the sides of the bowl. Scrape the batter into the prepared pan and smooth the surface evenly.</p>
<p>Bake for 30 to 40 minutes, or until a cake tester comes out clean. The cake should spring back when pressed lightly in the center. The cake should not shrink from the sides of the pan until after it is removed from the oven.</p>
<p>Let the cake cook on a wire rack for 10 minutes. Run a small metal spatula between the sides of the the pan and the cake. Invert the cake onto a lightly greased wire rack, then re-invert it to prevent splitting. Cook completely.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>42</td><td>grams</td><td>Dutch-processed cocoa powder, (1/2 c. + 1 Tbsp.)</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>boiling water</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>eggs, at room temp</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1 12</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>156</td><td>grams</td><td>cake flour, (1 1/3 cups)</td></tr> <tr><td>200</td><td>grams</td><td>superfine sugar, (1 cup)</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>133</td><td>grams</td><td>unsalted butter, (1 stick)</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>safflower oil</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Chocolate Layer Cake</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CinnamonPull-Aparts</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>

id : <TEXT>CinnamonRolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In a mixing bowl, cream together the sugar, salt, shortening and powered milk. If using a stand mixer, use the paddle attachment. Whip in the egg and lemon zest (or Fiori di Sicilia or lemon extract) until smooth. Add the flour, yeast and water (or milk). Mix on low speed until the dough forms a ball.</p>
<p>In the stand mixer, switch to the dough hook and mix on low for 2 minutes, then let the dough rest in the bowl for 10 minutes. Then, run the mixer on medium for approximately 10 minutes, until the dough is silky and supple, tacky but not sticky. If you prefer hand kneading: turn the dough out and knead it about 2 minutes, forming a ball. Let the ball rest for 10 minutes, then knead by hand for 12 to 15 minutes more. You may need to add a little flour or water to the dough while kneading.</p>
<p>Very lightly coat a bowl with oil then place the dough into; turn the dough to coat it. Cover the bowl and let the dough rise for about 2 hours until it is doubled. While the dough rises, mix the cinnamon sugar in a small jar or bowl. Prepare a sheet pan or baking sheet by lining it with baking parchment.</p>
<p>Mist the counter with spray oil and turn out the dough. With your hands and then a rolling pin, shape the dough into a square approximately 14" wide and 12"  deep. If you roll the dough out too thin, the cinnamon rolls will be tough.Cover the top of the dough with cinnamon sugar, from edge to edge.  Be generous and use it all. Roll up the dough toward you so that the resulting log is about 14" long. Pinch the seam closed and then turn it to the bottom. Cut the dough into 12 pieces and carefully place them in the pan. Place the buns about ½ inch apart.</p>
<p>To bake another day: Lightly spray the buns with cooking oil, then cover the pan with plastic wrap. Seal the edges, but leave some room for the dough to expand. Place the pan in the refrigerator for up to 2 days. Four hours before you want to cook, remove the pan from the refrigerator.</p>
<p>To bake today: Cover the dough loosely with plastic wrap and let rise for 75 to 90 minutes, until the buns have grown into each other and nearly doubled in size.</p>
<p>Thirty minutes before you want to cook, preheat the oven to 350 F. Bake the buns for 20 to 30 minutes, until golden brown. Cool in the pans for about 10 minutes.</p>
<p>While the buns cool, make the fondant: sift the powdered sugar into a bowl. Add the flavoring (vanilla, lemon extract, or nothing) and the milk, briskly whisking until all the sugar is dissolved. You may not need all of the milk, or you made need a tablespoon or two more. Make a thick, smooth paste.</p>
<p>Streak the glaze over the buns while they are warm, but not too hot. Once the glaze no longer runs, you can place the buns on a cooling rack. Wait at least 10 more minutes before serving for the best texture.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Dough</td></tr> <tr><td>3.25</td><td>ounces</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>2.75</td><td>ounces</td><td>shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg, slightly beaten</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>lemon zest</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>instant yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>16</td><td>ounces</td><td>bread flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>ounce</td><td>powdered milk</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>water, scant</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Cinnamon Sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1.5</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>ground cinnamon</td></tr> <tr><td>3.25</td><td>ounces</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>White Fondant Glaze</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>lemon extract</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>whole milk</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>cups</td><td>powdered sugar</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Cinnamon Rolls</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>For the dough, if you have it, use ¼ to ½ teaspoon of  Fiori di Sicilia instead of the lemon zest. You can also use lemon extract or lemon oil instead of the zest, but I think the lemon flavor is too strong; cut it back to about ½ tsp at most. And while the fondant also calls for lemon, I prefer to use vanilla extract if the lemon scent of the dough is strong. The hint of lemon and vanilla should be there, but it should not compete with the cinnamon. Use the best, freshest cinnamon you can get; it makes a difference. You can use butter instead of shortening if you prefer, but I think that shortening makes the better dough. And finally, if you don't want to use powdered milk, use a cup of milk instead of the water.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Adapted from The Break Bakers Apprentice</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>These are the very best cinnamon rolls. Specialty store cinnamon rolls do not compare. I make them for special occasions and sometimes just because Steve likes them so much.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>12 rolls</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CioccolatoGelato</TEXT>
categories : [ "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Mix milk powder, sugar, salt, cacao powder, and tapioca starch in a 2.5 quart saucepan. Add the cream and milk; whisk well until all dry ingredients have been incorporated. Whisk in corn syrup and egg yolks.</p>
<p>Put the chopped chocolate in a a glass or heatproof bowl that is large enough to contain the entire mixture. Set aside.</p>
<p>Begin cooking the base over medium-high heat, using a spatula to scrape the sides of the bowl. Whisk continuously to prevent any burning or clumping. Whisk slowly in the beginning; increase speed as mixture becomes warmer and begins to steam and thicken.</p>
<p>The mixture should thicken without boiling after 8 to 10 minutes; watch carefully so it doesn’t burn. Once the mixture coats the back of a spoon, continue to cook for 15 seconds longer, whisking vigorously; then immediately remove from heat.</p>
<p>Pour half of the hot mixture over the chopped chocolate, and whisk to allow the chocolate to melt and incorporate. Then whisk in the rest of the hot mixture, making sure all of the chocolate is fully melted and mixed in. (This can be a challenge to get the last bits of chocolate melted, but if you don’t they will be small bitter bits in the final product!)</p>
<p>Lay plastic wrap directly on the surface to prevent a skin from forming. Allow the mixture to sit about 45 minutes, until no longer hot. Place in the refrigerator to cool completely, about 4 hours.</p>
<p>Pour cold and thickened mixture into gelato machine or ice cream maker. Churn according to manufacturer’s directions. The gelato will expand and should churn until it is thick and creamy, but still soft enough to scoop into a storage container, about 30 - 55 minutes.</p>
<p>Place a piece of plastic directly on the gelato in the storage container. Top with an airtight lid and place in the refrigerator. Let the gelato freeze for at least 4-6 hours. It should be firm enough to scoop, but soft and creamy in texture.</p>
</TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>35</td><td>grams</td><td>dry milk powder</td></tr> <tr><td>225</td><td>grams</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>pinches</td><td>kosher salt</td></tr> <tr><td>30</td><td>grams</td><td>cacao powder</td></tr> <tr><td>20</td><td>grams</td><td>tapioca starch</td></tr> <tr><td>192</td><td>grams</td><td>heavy cream</td></tr> <tr><td>685</td><td>grams</td><td>whole milk</td></tr> <tr><td>40</td><td>grams</td><td>light corn syrup</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>egg yolks</td></tr> <tr><td>25</td><td>grams</td><td>100% dark chocolate, finely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>40</td><td>grams</td><td>60% dark chocolate, finely chopped</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Cioccolato Gelato</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Cacao powder is pure raw chocolate, but it isn’t commonly available. Substitute a natural, unsweetened cocoa powder.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The Art of Making Gelato</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I love this recipe. It makes a fairly dark chocolate gelato. You can vary its intensity by using different chocolate: I’ve been known to use all 63% chocolate, because that it is what I had, and it was great. It is a pain to chop the chocolate, but it needs to be pretty fine so that it will melt into the ice cream correctly. A food processor can help make sure it is well-chopped, just be careful not to melt it down too much. I use Guittard chocolate, but use any high quality chocolate that you like.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>1 quart</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CoconutCreamPie</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies", "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Prepare the crust</p>
<p>Combine and sift dry ingredients to mix thoroughly.  Cut in shortening until it is pea-sized; this crust has a lot of fat.  Add ice water by tablespoons, tossing the dough with a fork until it starts to hold together.  Press the dough into a rough disk and chill for at least 30 minutes.  Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>
<p>Roll out the crust and place in a 9-inch pie pan.  Bake for 10-15 minutes, until lightly browned.</p>
<p>Set aside to cool.</p>
<p>Prepare the filling</p>
<p>In a medium saucepan, combine the dry ingredients and mix thoroughly. Gradually stir in the coconut milk and the whole milk, making sure to avoid lumps. Place over medium heat and stir constantly until thick, making sure to scrape the bottom of the pan and avoid scorching. Reduce heat if needed; mixture should not boil.  This step will take around 20 minutes. The mixture should thickly coat a spoon when done.</p>
<p>Beat the egg yolks in a small bowl. Gradually add spoonfuls of the hot mixture while whisking constantly, until egg yolks are quite warm. Whisk the egg yolk mixture back into the saucepan. Stir in the shredded coconut. Cook for 2 more minutes.</p>
<p>Remove from heat; add extracts and butter. Beat until well mixed, then pour into cooled pie shell.</p>
<p>Top with meringue</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 375°F.</p>
<p>In a medium mixing bowl, beat egg whites with mixer until frothy.  While continuing to beat on high speed, sprinkle in the sugar by teaspoons.  Beat for several seconds after each addition.  Stop when all sugar is dissolved and soft peaks form.</p>
<p>Mound meringue over the hot pie filling, sealing to edge of crust.  Sprinkle shredded coconut over the top.  Bake about 10 minutes, until meringue is lightly browned and coconut is toasted.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Crust</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>tablespoon</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cup</td><td>shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>6 - 7</td><td>tablespoons</td><td>ice water</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Filling</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/3</td><td>cup</td><td>cornstarch</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>coconut milk</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>whole milk</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td></td><td>egg yolks</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>coconut, shredded</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>coconut extract</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>tablespoon</td><td>butter</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Meringue</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td></td><td>egg whites</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>tablespoons</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/3</td><td>cup</td><td>coconut, shredded</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "Pie", "Coconut" ]
title : <TEXT>Coconut Cream Pie</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You can substitute additional vanilla extract for the coconut extract.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Lisa Guinn</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I make this pie because Steve likes coconut better than chocolate or lemon. It took a couple of attempts to get this recipe just right. For the shredded coconut, I use the best and freshest unsweetened coconut I can find, but you could use sweetened coconut if you prefer. You could also use coconut cream instead of coconut milk: you will find coconut cream with the cocktail mixes in the grocery store. Finally, I use the whole can of coconut milk, and then add regular milk to make 3 cups.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>9" pie</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CoolRiseSweetBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads", "thanksgiving", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Dissolve yeast in water in a large warm bowl. Add milk, sugar, salt, margarine, eggs, and 3 cups flour. Beat with a wooden spoon or electric mixer (low speed) until smooth. Beat vigorously (medium speed) until thick and elastic, about 3 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir in 2 cups flour, adding more if needed, to make a soft dough that leaves the sides of the bowl. Turn dough out onto floured surface and divide in half. Knead each half for 5 minutes, or until smooth and elastic.</p>
<p>Cover and let sit for 20 minutes.</p>
<p>Punch down and shape as desired; place in greased pans. Refrigerate for 2 to 48 hours.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 375°F.</p>
<p>When ready to cook, break surface bubbles with an oiled toothpick. Let rolls stand at room temperature for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Bake rolls for 25 minutes, using a lower oven rack position. Remove from pans and brush with margarine.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CornbreadDressing</TEXT>
categories : [ "thanksgiving", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 350°F. Combine seasoning mix ingredients in a small cup. Set aside.</p>
<p>In a large skillet, melt butter and margarine with onion, bell pepper, celery, garlic, and bay leaves over high heat. Sauté 2 minutes, stirring occasionally. Add seasoning mix to skillet and sauté about 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir in Tabasco and stock. Cook for 5 more minutes, stirring frequently.</p>
<p>Add cornbread, milk, and eggs, stirring well. Turn off heat. Pour into a greased 9 x 13 inch pan.</p>
<p>Bake until browned on top, 35 to 40 minutes.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CrispyWafers</TEXT>
categories : [ "appetizerssnacks" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>
<p>Mix dry ingredients together in  a medium bowl. Add 2 tablespoons margarine, water and vinegar; mix thoroughly. Knead for a minute or two in the bowl until the mixture forms a stiff dough.</p>
<p>Grease your hands and shape the dough into a 12-inch cylinder. Slice the roll into 16 pieces. For each cracker, spread ¼ teaspoon of seeds on the counter; press the dough into the seeds. Roll the cracker into a paper-thin wafer. Spread another ¼ teaspoon of seeds on the top of the cracker. Turn the cracker over and place on an ungreased baking sheet.</p>

servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>CroustadeofMushrooms</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 375°F. Set aside a few slivered almonds for garnish. Mix together the ground and slivered almonds, bread crumbs, onions, garlic, and 6 tablespoons butter. id : <TEXT>Daddy'sFudge</TEXT>
categories : [ "desserts", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine cocoa, sugar, and salt in a large cast-iron pot.</p>
<p>Add milk gradually, stirring. Bring to bubbly boil over high heat, stirring constantly.</p>
<p>Reduce heat to medium and boil without stirring until 232°F is reached (soft ball stage). Be patient; this takes a while; I estimate about 20 minutes.  However, once the temperature gets close, it tends to rise quickly. An accurate instant-read thermometer is a big help.</p>
<p>Remove from heat. Drop in butter and vanilla. Add peanut butter.  DO NOT STIR. Allow to cool to 110°F- you should be able to place your hand comfortably on the bottom of the pan. Be patient again, as this can take 45 minutes or more! (An infrared thermometer gun is really helpful here.)</p>
<p>Beat until fudge thickens and loses its gloss. Quickly pour and spread in a buttered 8-inch square pan or glass pie plate.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2/3</td><td>cups</td><td>cocoa powder</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>cups</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/8</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>milk</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>smooth peanut butter, approximately</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Daddy's Fudge</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You can omit the peanut butter. With the peanut butter, the fudge will be softer and creamier.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>36</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Dick Monk</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>When I was growing up, my father cooked only a few things at our house: fried fish, peanut brittle, and this fudge. My mother did all the rest of the cooking. Later in life, when their kids were grown, Daddy took over more of the cooking duties from Mama. As a child, I loved to "clean up" the cooking pan after the fudge was made. I would take a spoon and scrape out every last bit of fudge from the cast iron pan.  I still do it when I cook fudge, and I still use a big deep cast iron skillet just like Daddy did.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>DinnerPartyChickenKiev</TEXT>
categories : [ "chicken"  ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Blend cream in a blender on a lower speed until thick. While blending, add ice water (it should be very cold). increase blender speed and process for 1-2 minutes longer.  (Note that a food processor does not do this job very well.)</p>
<p>Strain the water from the butter. Blend in the lemon juice, salt, white pepper, parsley, chives and tarragon.</p>
<p>Shape butter into a 3-inch by 4-inch rectangle on waxed paper; chill until firm.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, beat the eggs with 2 teaspoons of water until slightly foamy.</p>
<p>Place bread crumbs in a shallow dish.</p>
<p>Pound chicken breasts between plastic until ¼-inch thick.</p>
<p>Cut butter into eight ½-inch slices. Place a slice of butter on each breast and roll up, tucking in sides to seal completely. Roll breasts in flour; shake to remove excess. Coat with egg mixture and then roll in bread crumbs, patting lightly. Wrap gently in plastic. Refrigerate for at least 1 hour. (You can refrigerate for up to 24 hours.)</p>
<p>Fry chicken, 4 rolls at a time, in deep hot oil for 5 minutes. Keep warm while frying remaining breasts. Serve immediately.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>8</td><td></td><td>chicken breast halves without skin, boned</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>heavy cream</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>ice water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>lemon juice</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/8</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>white pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>fresh parsley, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>fresh chives, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dried tarragon</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>eggs</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>fresh bread crumbs</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ ]
title : <TEXT>Dinner Party Chicken Kiev</TEXT>

servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT></TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>Dumplings</TEXT>
categories : [ "basics", "quickbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Sift together flour, baking powder and salt. Cut in shortening until the mixture resembles coarse cornmeal.</p>
<p>If you want a more biscuit-like dumpling, use only ¾ cup milk. Roll or pat out dough and cut it into the desired shape. I usually make strips about 1 x 4-inch.</p>
<p>If you want a drop dumpling, use the full cup of milk. The dough will be easier to work with if you dip your spoon into the hot stew before spooning up each dumpling.</p>
<p>Drop dumplings into simmering stew, making sure that each lands on a piece of meat or vegetable -- dumplings should not be immersed.  (I don''t always follow this rule exactly.) Cover pot and cook for 12 to 15 minutes, without removing cover.</p>
<p>To make Chicken and Dumplings, I just boil some chicken and pick the meat from the bone in chunks; toss the water. Cut up as much celery and onion as you like, relative to the amount of chicken you have. Sauté the celery and onion in a little oil until soft. Add the chicken. Add enough stock to cover the ingredients, plus about an inch more. (Use good stock, not the water the chicken was boiled in.) Season to taste with salt, pepper, marjoram, thyme or whatever you like. Bring to a boil, then add dumplings and cook as directed.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>flour, sifted</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>milk</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>minced parsley, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dried thyme, optional</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Dumplings</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You may use any herbs that you like, in any combination.  About ¼ tsp. of each herb should be enough for these dumplings.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Good Housekeeping, 1944</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>If you don't want to make dumplings from scratch, you can take a big shortcut: buy the cheapest (and oldest) refrigerated biscuits you can find in the store. Stay away from biscuits that have layers of butter; stick with the plainest biscuits you can buy. Open the package and roll each biscuit flat with a rolling pin.  Cut into strips and drop into stew.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>FigPreserves</TEXT>
categories : [ "basics" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Sort figs; use ripe figs but not cracked ones. Peel the figs with a sharp knife.  (If you do not peel figs, clean the skins: cover the figs with hot water and bring it to a boil.  Remove from heat and let stand 3-4 minutes.  Drain.) Stir together the sugar and water in a large heavy pot. Stir over medium heat until sugar is dissolved. Increase heat and bring to a boil for 4 minutes. Add lemon and figs. Cook over medium heat, at a gentle and steady boil, until clear and translucent -- about 1½ hours. Do not stir; do not scrap the bottom; do not shake the pot. Fill hot, sterilized jars with boiling figs and syrup to within ½ inch of the top. Use a small spatula (or other nonmetallic utensil) to release any air bubbles. Wipe sealing edge and seal. Process in a boiling water bath for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Canning notes: I suggest that you use pint jars for this.  You can reuse old jars, but not old lids. Place 8 jars in a pot that is at least 3 inches deeper than the jars. Fill the jars and the pot with cool water to the top of the jars.  Cover and bring to a simmer over medium heat, but do not boil. Place 8 new flat lids in a small saucepan and cover with water.   Cover and bring to a simmer over medium heat, but do not boil.  Do not heat the screw bands. Fill one jar at a time.  Remove jar from canner with tongs; pour the water from the jar back into the canner.  Do not dry the jar.  Place the jar on a tray.  Fill the jar as directed above. Screw on the band, using only your fingers, until resistance is met.  Then tighten down using only your fingertips.  Do not use any tools, or over-tighten the band.  Return jar to canning pot. When all jars are filled, cover pot and bring to a full rolling boil.  Do not start the timer until water is boiling rapidly. At the end of the processing time, remove lid, turn off heat and wait 5 minutes.  Remove jars without tilting them.  Place jars on a towel in a draft-free place and let rest undisturbed for 24 hours. After 24 hours, check lids for seal: remove screw bands and press down on the center of each lid with your finger.  Sealed lids will be concave (they will curve downward) and will not move when pressed with your finger.  Jars that did not seal must be refrigerated immediately.  If desired, put screw bands back on the jars, loosely.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>quarts</td><td>figs, peeled or unpeeled</td></tr> <tr><td>8</td><td>cups</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>medium</td><td>lemon, sliced and seeded</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Fig Preserves</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>64</TEXT>
source : <TEXT></TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I believe that I have finally located a recipe on the internet that will reproduce my Grandma Monk's fig preserves. To be honest, I haven't tried it yet. I once asked her how she made her preserves and she said "Make a simple syrup with sugar, add the figs and lemon. Then can it."  That's not a quote, but it's close.  So I know that this recipe has the right ingredients.  She might have used a little more lemon, though. And I have seen other recipes that use only 6 cups of sugar. I am sure that she did not peel her figs.  Use ripe figs from Arkansas or Louisiana; they are yellow-green and available in July and August.  I don't know the name of the variety. Her figs were light brown in the jar and unbroken; the insides of the figs were the same color as the outside.</p>
<p>This recipe promises to deliver the whole fruit in a syrup about the consistency of honey.  That sounds like her preserves!</p>
<p>The yield is just an estimate. If you don't have enough jars, place any leftover preserves in an airtight container and refrigerate it.  Use them within a few weeks.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>4 quarts</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>FlakyPastry</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Measure flour into sifter over medium bowl.  Add salt and sift into bowl.</p>
<p>Drop shortening into the flour; cut in with pastry blender until particles are the size of small peas.</p>
<p>Sprinkle 1 tablespoon of water over a small portion of the flour mixture. Lightly press together moistened particles with a fork. Toss this dough aside. Repeat until all flour is moistened. Be careful to add water to a dry spot. Use just enough water to make particles stick together.</p>
<p>With hands, lightly form the pastry into one ball.  Wrap ball in plastic and chill ½ hour.</p>
<p>If a cooked pie shell is needed: Form dough into crust, then chill several minutes or prick all over with fork. Bake in a preheated 450°F oven to 15-18 minutes. Cool thoroughly before filling.</p>
<p>This recipe makes a two-crust pie shell, either 8-inch or 9-inch.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>FreshAsparagusRolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "appetizerssnacks" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Steam asparagus until crisp-tender, about 4 minutes. Immerse in cold water. Drain, then dry thoroughly.</p>
<p>Remove crusts from bread. Roll between sheets of waxed paper. Brush each bread slice with melted butter, then sprinkle with cheese. Place an asparagus spear diagonally across each slice of bread and roll up. Place rolls on baking sheet with exposed corner of bread down. Crowd rolls together or use toothpicks to prevent unrolling. (Recipe can be refrigerated for 1 day at this point.)</p>
<p>Brush with melted butter and sprinkle with more cheese. Dust with paprika. Bake 10-12 minutes at 400°F. Remove toothpicks and sprinkle with parsley. Serve hot.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>GingerbreadHouses</TEXT>
categories : [ "cookiesandbars" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Basic Gingerbread:</p>
<p>In a large bowl, sift together flour and ginger; make a well in center. In a saucepan over medium-low heat, combine butter, molasses and brown sugar. Cook, stirring constantly, until thoroughly melted, about 3-4 minutes. Stir in baking soda until blended. Add liquids and eggs to the well in the flour. Stir until thoroughly blended. On a lightly floured surface, knead mixture to form a smooth dough, about 1 minute. Divide dough into thirds. Wrap each piece separately and refrigerate until slightly firm, a minimum of 30 minutes. Dough can be refrigerated for up to 48 hours. Continue with the "Baking the House" section below.</p>
<p>Old-Fashioned Gingerbread:</p>
<p>In a large bowl, sift together flour, baking soda, salt, and spices. In the bowl of an electric mixer, combine shortening, sugar, molasses and eggs. Beat on medium speed until smooth and blended, 3 to 4 minutes. Reduce speed to medium-low; add flour mixture and beat until blended, another 3 to 4 minutes. Divide dough in thirds. Wrap each piece separately and refrigerate until slightly firm, a minimum of 30 minutes. Dough can be refrigerated for up to 48 hours. Continue with the "Baking the House" section below.</p>
<p>Baking the House:</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°Ffor at least 30 minutes. To create one gingerbread house, bake the side walls once and the front-back walls/room section twice, using 1/3 of dough each time. With a pastry brush, thoroughly grease the plaque before baking. Beginning in the center of each mold and working out to the corners, press the dough with your fingers. Press thoroughly into the relief to prevent air pockets from forming. Bake until gingerbread is cooked through and pulls away from the edges, about 20 to 25 minutes. Cool 10 minutes in plaque - be patient! Turn gingerbread out of plaque and carefully invert, relief side down, onto a wire rack to cool at least 1 hour. Repeat with remaining dough -- let plaque cool completely before the next round.</p>
<p>Royal Icing:</p>
<p>This is the cement that holds the house together. Do not make it before you are ready to begin house construction. In the bowl of an electric mixer, combine all ingredients. Beat on medium-high until mixture forms still peaks and is nearly triple in volume. This will take 7-8 minutes. (Use a stand mixer if you have one, because this is a long time to hold a mixer.) Cover tightly with plastic wrap to prevent drying and store at room temperature.</p>
<p>Building the House:</p>
<p>All pieces of the house should be completely cool. It is best if the pieces rest a day, because they do sometimes shrink or warp a little. Prepare the Royal Icing. With a sharp knife, lightly "shave" the sides of each wall to create smooth, flush edges. Fit a pastry bag with a small tip, and fill it with icing. Apply a thin ribbon of icing (about 1/8 inch thick) along the edge of a side wall. With the pattern facing out, join the side wall to the front/back wall to form a right angle and a flush corner. Hold firmly until the icing hardens and the walls bond -- about 1 to 2 minutes. Let this piece sit for 7 to 8 minutes more.  While waiting, repeat with the other two pieces. You will have two L-shaped pieces. Apply a ribbon of icing to the remaining edges and carefully join the 2 L-shaped pieces. Hold firmly until the icing hardens, 1 to 2 minutes. Reinforce the inside corners with additional icing. Let set 7 to 8 minutes Add the roof: apply a thin ribbon of icing around the top edges of each wall. One piece at a time, place the roof sections, curved side down, on top of the house and hold firmly until they bond and the icing hardens, about 2 minutes. Let sit for 7-8 minutes. Build the chimney: Apply a dot of icing to both sides of the non-relief chimney piece. Join the remaining two chimney pieces, relief-sides facing out, to either side of the iced piece and hold firmly until they bond, 1 to 2 minutes. To attach the chimney to the root, apply 2-3 dots of icing to the underside and place on top of the roof next to the side with chimney design. Allow the house to set at leave 30 minutes before decorating. You may wish to pipe additional icing along the exposed seams for decoration and additional strength. Wait 30 minutes before doing this as you are adding weight to the structure. I recommend that you wait at least 24 hours before decorating if you have added more icing.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Basic Gingerbread</td></tr> <tr><td>5</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>ground ginger</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cup</td><td>unsalted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1/3</td><td>cup</td><td>molasses</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>dark brown sugar, packed</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>baking soda</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>large</td><td>eggs, lightly beaten</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Old Fashioned Gingerbread</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>ground nutmeg</td></tr> <tr><td>5</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>baking soda</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>ground cloves</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>ground cinnamon</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>ground ginger</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>shortening, melted and cooled</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>molasses</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>eggs, lightly beaten</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Royal Icing</td></tr> <tr><td>4 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>confectioner's sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cream of tartar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>pinch</td><td>salt</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Gingerbread Houses</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>0</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Williams-Sonoma</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Yes, this is the gingerbread for making houses. It is very time-consuming and I haven’t done it in a long time.</p>
<p>Be sure to start this the WEEK before you want to decorate. The gingerbread needs to sit up for a day before you construct the house, and then the house needs to sit for at least a day before you decorate.  So it's best to have a weekend for construction and then a weekend for decoration. Do not short-cut the steps or the hardening time, or things will fall apart.</p>
<p>I have a mold, and I don't know how you would do this without one! Use either the Basic Gingerbread or the Old Fashion Gingerbread recipe to make the walls.  Since you probably aren't going to eat this fresh, or even at all, who cares?</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>
