id : <TEXT>GlutenFreeDinnerRolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Lightly grease a 12-muffin pan. (Use a pan for standard size muffins or cupcakes). Dust the pan with some gluten-free flour (or use rice flour). Shake off excess flour carefully.</p>
<p>Mix all dry ingredients in a large bowl. Quickly add buttermilk, egg and melted butter. Mix until just blended.</p>
<p>Scrape bowl and beaters and then beat at high speed for 3 minutes. Spoon dough into muffin pan and use a lightly oiled spoon to smooth the tops of the rolls (they don't need to be perfect). If desired, sprinkle rolls with sesame seeds or poppy seeds at this time - mash them slightly into the rolls as you smooth the tops. Cover the muffin pan and let the rolls rise in a warm place for 30-40 minutes, until the the dough is almost to the top of the pan. Do not let the rolls rise too much or they will be unstable.</p>
<p>While rolls are rising, place a shelf in the center of the oven. Preheat oven to 400°F for at least 20 minutes. (Do not use a convection oven; it will brown the rolls too quickly.)</p>
<p>Bake rolls for about 20 minutes. Test a roll with an instant-read thermometer - the center should read 205°F. Remove rolls from pan and place on a rack to cool. Brush the tops with melted butter, if desired.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>gluten-free flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>xanthan gum</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 </td><td>teaspoon</td><td>unflavored gelatin</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>pkg</td><td>active dry yeast, not quick-rise</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>eggs, at room temp</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>unsalted butter, melted and cooled</td></tr> <tr><td>7/8</td><td>cup</td><td>buttermilk, heated to 110°F</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "gluten-free"  ]
title : <TEXT>Gluten-Free Dinner Rolls</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>To save the rolls: Wait until the rolls are completely cool, which will take at least 4 hours. Wrap each roll individually and completely in aluminum foil. Place the rolls in an airtight bag, expelling as much air as possible. Keep them in the refrigerator and reheat as needed.</p>
<p>This recipe will work equally well with buttermilk powder instead of buttermilk. Add the powder to the dry ingredients and use water in place of the buttermilk.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Gluten-Free Baking Classics</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is a great recipe for gluten-free rolls; it is as quicker and easier than most regular roll recipes. It does require a few special ingredients, but these are things you will want to keep on hand if you are baking gluten-free. I use King Arthur Flour's brand of gluten-free flour and find it excellent if a bit expensive. Xanthan gum is a powder that can be purchased from King Arthur, but can be found in many other places.</p>
<p>Yes, you can buy many gluten-free breads now, but I think there is something special about cooking your own. Especially at the holidays, when folks with allergies are often denied the family's favorite foods, this is a small effort that can make them feel included and appreciated.</p>
<p>Gluten-free breads do not keep well; this is another reason that it can be better to bake than to buy. </p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>12 rolls</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>GlutenFreeYellowCake</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies"]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 350°F. Lightly grease a 9" round cake pan.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, whisk together the flour, xanthin gum and cake enhancer.</p>
<p>In a medium bowl (or your stand mixer), beat together the sugar, butter, salt, vanilla and baking powder until smooth. Add one egg and beat for several minute until fluffy. Scrape the sides and bottom of the bowl, then beat in the second egg. Scrape the sides and bottom of the bowl again.</p>
<p>Beat in the milk alternately with the dry ingredients, adding about ⅓ each time. Begin and end with the dry ingredients. Pour the batter into the prepared pan.</p>
<p>Bake the cake for 20 to 25 minutes, until a cake tester tests clean. Remove from oven.</p>
<p>Cool for 5 to 10 minutes before turning the cake out of the pan to cool on a rack. </p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>GoldenPullApartButterBuns</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine all ingredients in a large bowl. Mix and knead until you have a soft, smooth dough. You can use a stand mixer, a bread machine, your hands or whatever. Place the dough in a lightly greased container that can hold 8 cups. Let the dough rise for 60 to 90 minutes, until it is almost doubled in bulk.</p>
<p>Lightly grease two 8-inch cake pans. Gently deflate the dough and place it on a lightly greased work surface. Divide it into 16 equal pieces. Round each piece into a smooth ball. Space 8 rolls in each pan.</p>
<p>Cover the rolls and let them rise until they are crowded and puffy, about 60 to 90 minutes. During the last 15 minutes of rising, preheat the oven to 350°F.</p>
<p>Bake the rolls for 22 to 24 minutes, until golden brown. Remove from oven and brush with melted butter. After a minute or two, turn the rolls out onto a cooling rack.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>GoodEatsMeatloaf</TEXT>
categories : [ "beef" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 425°F. In a food processor, combine croutons and spices. Pulse until mixture is a fine texture. Dump into a large bowl.</p>
<p>Now combine the onion, carrot (break it up a bit), garlic and red bell pepper in the food processor. Pulse until finely chopped, but not pureed. Combine this with the meat and the croutons in the large bowl. Season with salt and add the egg. Combine thoroughly, but avoid squeezing or mashing the meat. Pack the mixture into a 10-inch loaf pan to mold the shape of the meat.</p>
<p>Turn the meatloaf out onto a sheet pan (with edges) that has been lined with paper. Insert a temperature probe into the meat at a 45 degree angle. Make sure that the tip is in the middle and not touching the pan. Set the probe for 155°F. Place the meatloaf in the oven.</p>
<p>Combine the glaze ingredients. Brush the glaze onto the meatloaf after it has cooked for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>The meatloaf should cook about 45 minutes. Let it rest for 10 minutes before cutting.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>GoodEatsRoastTurkey</TEXT>
categories : [ "thanksgiving" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine all brine ingredients, except ice water, in a stockpot. Bring to a boil. Stir to dissolve solids. Remove from heat and cool to room temperature, then refrigerate until thoroughly chilled. Early on the day of cooking (or late the night before), combine the brine and ice water in a clean 5-gallon bucket. Place thawed turkey breast side done in brine and cover. Refrigerate, or place in a cool area (like a basement) for 6 hours. Turn turkey over once, halfway through brining. [I put the turkey in a "turkey cooking bag" along with the brine.  I place the bag in an ice chest and put it in the coolest part of the house.]</p>
<p>A few minutes before roasting, heat the over to 500°F. Combine the apple, onion, cinnamon stick and cup of water in a microwave-safe dish. Microwave on high for 5 minutes. Remove bird from brine. Rinse it inside and out with cold water. Pat dry with paper towels. Discard brine. Place bird on roasting rack. Add steeped aromatics to cavity along with rosemary and sage. Tuck back wings and coat whole bird liberally with canola oil. Roast on lowest level of the oven at 500°F for 30 minutes. Remove from oven and cover breast with double layer of aluminum foil. Insert probe thermometer into thickest part of the breast and return to oven. Reduce oven to 350°F. Set thermometer alarm (if you have that feature) to 161°F.</p>
<p>A 14 to 16 pound bird should require a total of 2 to 2 ½ hours of roasting. Let turkey rest, loosely covered, for 15 minutes before carving.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>16</td><td>lbs.</td><td>turkey, thawed</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Brine:</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>kosher salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>light brown sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>gallon</td><td>vegetable stock</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>black peppercorns</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>allspice berries</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>gallon</td><td>water, iced</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>medium</td><td>cinnamon stick</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>candied ginger root</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>For the aromatics:</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>medium</td><td>red apple, sliced</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>medium</td><td>onion, sliced</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>sprigs</td><td>rosemary</td></tr> <tr><td>6</td><td>sprigs</td><td>sage</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>canola oil</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "turkey" ]
title : <TEXT>Good Eats Roast Turkey</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Alton prefers frozen turkeys, because they are less likely to be bruised in the shipping process. If you are in a rush, you can thaw a turkey using the water drip method. Turn on the faucet to a quick drip using COLD water.  Set the frozen bird under the drip, still in its plastic wrapping. It will still take a few hours to thaw the bird, but not days. (Do not cheat and use hot water - the bird will not thaw much faster and it will gradually cook the meat under the drip - yuck.)</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Alton Brown</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is Alton Brown's recipe for great Thanksgiving turkey. However, I only use this recipe for brining the turkey. I still prefer to cook the turkey with my "original" recipe. </p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>HamBall</TEXT>
categories : [ "appetizerssnacks" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Mix together all ingredients, except the coating, in a food processor. Shape the mixture into a ball, and roll in your choice of coating. This is a very sticky mixture, and can be challenging to shape!</p>
<p>My shaping technique: place some of the almonds on a small piece of parchment paper. Carefully scrape the mixture on top of the almonds, trying to shape it into a ball as much as possible. Chilling the mixture for an hour at this point may help. Pat the almonds onto the top and sides of the ball. Find a bowl that will hold at least half of the mixture; I use a cereal bowl. As best you can, line the bowl with almonds. Carefully turn the ham ball into the bowl and use the bowl to shape it. Pat with almonds and rotate until you have used up all the almonds. Place the bowl in the refrigerator; turn out onto a pretty dish to serve.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>Hard-boiledEggs</TEXT>
categories : [ "cheeseandeggs" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>For the InstantPot:</p>
<p>Place a rack in the pot; I like to use a silicone basket that is easy to remove when done.  Pour in the water and place eggs in the rack. Close and lock the lid; make sure the pressure valve is set to Sealing. Press Manual or Pressure Cook (depending on the model). Select High Pressure. Set the time to 5 minutes.</p>
<p>When the cooking cycle ends, set a time for 5 more minutes. Then vent the pressure.</p>
<p>Press Cancel and remove the lid. Transfer the eggs to a medium bowl of cold water with ice. Allow the eggs to cool 5 minutes in the water. Adjust time if you want a softer yolk.</p>
<p>Manual method:</p>
<p>Bring eggs to room temperature. (Variations in starting temperature affect how the eggs cook.)</p>
<p>Pierce the large end of each egg with a pin to let air escape.</p>
<p>Fill a pot with enough water to cover the eggs - but don’t add eggs yet. Bring the water to a boil and then add eggs.</p>
<p>Simmer approximately 8 minutes for soft-boiled, or 12 minutes for hard-boiled.</p>
<p>Transfer the eggs to a medium bowl of cold water with ice. Allow the eggs to cool 5 minutes in the water.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>6</td><td>large</td><td>eggs</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td> cup</td><td>water</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Hard-boiled Eggs</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT></TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>The InstantPot makes great hard-boiled eggs and does it very consistently. This recipe provides instructions for both the InstaPot and manually.</p>
<p>Regardless  of technique, older eggs will peel easier than fresh eggs.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>HighProteinChallah</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Dissolve yeast in water in a large bowl. Add salt, honey, butter, and oil; stir well. Beat in all but 2 tablespoons of the eggs (reserve for egg wash).</p>
<p>In a separate bowl, combine milk powder and flour. Stir flour gradually into the liquid until it is dry enough to begin kneading.  You may not need it all.</p>
<p>Knead dough until smooth and elastic. Let rise until doubled. Shape into 3 loaves.</p>
<p>Let rise again. Brush the loaves with the reserved egg just before baking.</p>
<p>Bake in a preheated 350°F oven for 30-35 minutes.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>HolidayButterCookies</TEXT>
categories : [ "cookiesandbars" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine sugar, butter, egg yolk, salt and flavor; beat until smooth.</p>
<p>Add the flour, mixing until smooth. The mixture will seem dry at first, but will suddenly come together. If it doesn't, dribble in up to a tablespoon of water.</p>
<p>Divide the dough in half. Shape each half into a flattened disk and wrap in plastic. Refrigerate for 2 hours or overnight.</p>
<p>When ready to bake, preheat oven to 350 degrees F and remove disks from refrigerator. Let disks warm up for 20 to 30 minutes until soft enough to roll. The dough will be cold, but not rock hard.</p>
<p>Sprinkle work surface and rolling pin with flour. Roll out a disk to ⅛" to 3/16" thick. Cut shapes with cookie cutter. Place close together on ungreased cookie sheet - these cookies spread very little. (Tip: use parchment paper to remove cookies easily between batches.)</p>
<p>Bake cookies for 12 to 14 minutes, until set and barely brown at the edges. Cool cookies on the pan (or slide parchment off onto rack). Do not try to move cookies until they have set and cooled slightly. When cookies are completely cool, ice and decorate.</p>
<p>Icing: combine sugar, milk and corn syrup to make a soft, smooth, spreadable icing. The icing should go on thick, but settle into a smooth surface in about 30 minutes. Test it and adjust as needed. It is easier to add more milk than it is to add more sugar. But don't wait until the icing hardens to decorate the cookies!</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Cookies</td></tr> <tr><td>5</td><td>ounces</td><td>confectioner's sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>9</td><td>ounces</td><td>salted butter, at room temp</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg yolk</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>Fiori di Sicilia</td></tr> <tr><td>11 ½</td><td>ounces</td><td>unbleached flour</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Icing</td></tr> <tr><td>10</td><td>ounces</td><td>confectioner's sugar, or glazing sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>ounces</td><td>light corn syrup</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>milk, + up to 1 tsp additional</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Holiday Butter Cookies</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>If you are using unsalted butter, increase the salt to 1 teaspoon total. Instead of the Fiori di Sicilia, you can use 2 teaspoons vanilla extract or 1 teaspoon almond extract. If you want to use a stronger flavor, like lemon extract or butter rum, start with ⅛ teaspoon and flavor to taste. You can also use ½ teaspoon of finely grated lemon peel.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>16</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>King Arthur Flour</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is a replacement for the rolled sugar cookie recipe that I used to use for making Christmas cookies. I like to make the cookies and then decorate them with friends and family. The first dozen cookies are usually carefully decorated with traditional motifs - blue eyes and red mouths on the gingerbread men, for example. But by the last dozen, strange-looking cookies are produced as we get bored and start trying to use up all the frosting. I have a multi-decade collection of metal cookie cutters.</p>
<p>These cookies are a bit brittle if rolled thin, but they are very tasty. They cut into cookies easily and are good to decorate, too. In addition to decorating after cooking, try sprinkling some colored sugar on the cookies before you bake them.</p></TEXT>

notes : <TEXT></TEXT>

time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>You can use white pepper instead of cayenne if you prefer. Black pepper makes the sauce look very unappealing. You can use margarine instead of butter for this sauce, but if you are really concerned about cholesterol, you shouldn't be making this sauce anyway!</p>
<p>You must serve this sauce immediately after it is made. It will curdle if left on the stove, and it will develop a skin if it cools down too much. I think the trick to Hollandaise is patience; you are emulsifying the butter and the egg yolk, and the slower you melt the butter, the better.</p></TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Prepare ice cream mixture. Chill. Place ice cream in can with dasher. Assemble freezer.</p>

id : <TEXT>InstantPotChickenandDumplings</TEXT>
categories : [ "soups" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Save the leafy tops from the celery when you chop it.</p>
<p>Hit Sauté” n the Instant Pot; adjust if needed so it’s on the “More” setting. Add in the butter. Once melted, add in the onion, carrots, and celery; sauté for 5 minutes. Add the garlic and sauté for 1 minute longer.</p>
<p>Pour in the stock and stir well. Add the chicken and make sure it is covered by the stock. Toss the in the bay leaves and secure the lid. Hit “Cancel” and then hit “Pressure Cook.”  Set it for High Pressure for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>When the chicken is done cooking, perform a quick release. Discard the bay leaves and remove the chicken from pot with tongs. Set chicken aside in a bowl to cool. Add the sherry, seasoned salt, poultry seasoning, pepper, rubbed sage, thyme parsley, and the leafy celery tops to the InstantPot; stir well. Let the pot rest for the time being</p>
<p>While the chicken cools, make the dumplings: Put the flour, baking powder, and salt in a mixing bowl and whisk together.  In a pyrex dish, combine the butter and milk; microwave for 40 seconds. Pour the milk/butter mixture into the flour and lightly mix with a fork until totally blended so a warm dough forms. (NOTE: Don’t overdo the mixing as it can make for a tough dumpling). Lightly knead the dough. Then, on a clean surface covered with flour, take a flour-coated rolling pin and roll the dough to be 1/8″ thick max. (It is very important to keep the dumplings thin so they will cook properly).Using a pizza cutter or a knife, slice the dough vertically into strips about 1” wide and then slice horizontally about 2” wide, forming little rectangular strips. Dust with additional flour so the strips don’t stick to each other.</p>
<p>Turn the InstantPot back on: hit “Sauté” and make sure it is on “High” setting. Once the stock bubbles, stir in the cornstarch slurry. When it returns to a boil, add the dumpling strips one-by-one and then give them a good stir making sure none are sticking to each other. Cover and simmer for 10 minutes.  (NOTE: Use a glass lid if you have it. If you use the pressure-cooking lid, do not let it seal. Rest it slightly off-kilter on the pot as it may come to pressure otherwise – even with the valve in “venting” position.)</p>
<p>After dumplings have cooked for 10 minutes, hit “Cancel” so the bubbles die down.</p>
<p>The chicken should now be relatively should be cool enough to handle. Pick out all the meat, discarding the bones, skin, and cartilage. Rip the chicken by hand into robust pieces and add to the pot. Add in the heavy cream and give everything a final stir until well combined.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>4</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>salted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>medium</td><td>yellow onion, diced</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>carrots, diced</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>stalks</td><td>celery, slice in 1/4" pieces</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>garlic, crushed</td></tr> <tr><td>6</td><td>cups</td><td>chicken stock</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>whole</td><td>bay leaves</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>Sherry wine, (or use more stock)</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>seasoning salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>poultry seasoning</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>black pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>rubbed sage</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dried thyme</td></tr> <tr><td>3 ½</td><td>lbs.</td><td>chicken pieces</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Slurry</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>cornstarch</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>heavy cream</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Dumplings</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>salted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>milk</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "InstantPot" ]
title : <TEXT>InstantPot Chicken and Dumplings</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>InstantPotRedBeansandRice</TEXT>
categories : [ "beansandpeas", "soups" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Soak beans overnight in water to cover.</p>
<p>Drain and rinse beans. Put all ingredients in the Instant Pot. Set the pot on Pressure Cook for 30 minutes. (It will take longer than 30 minutes, because the pot has to come up to pressure.) Use the instant pressure release. This recipe does not make a sauce, but you may want to reduce the liquid by simmering on Slow Cook with the lid off.</p>
<p>Serve by ladling ½ cup of beans over ⅔ cup of hot cooked rice. (Rice is cooked separately.)</p></TEXT>

tags : [ "InstantPot" ]
title : <TEXT>InstantPot Red Beans and Rice</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Important - the ham for this recipe should be baked, not smoked!  Look for the term "uncured" or even better,  "seasoning ham." I used to  make this recipe with a good bony pork shoulder cut (and I didn't need a ham bone). Now I can find uncured, bone-in ham at the local natural foods store -- it works great!</p>
<p>You may substitute salt pork for the pickled pork (which you probably won't be able to find) - if you do, omit the salt.</p>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 375°F.</p>

id : <TEXT>JessicasFreshTomatoSoup</TEXT>
categories : [ "soups" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Start a small pot of water boiling, to blanch the tomatoes. While you are waiting for the water to boil, chop the onion, garlic and green onions. In a large pan, sauté the onion in the olive oil. When it begins to soften, add the garlic and green onions. Cook until the mixture is softened but not browned. When the water begins to boil, use tongs to add a tomato to the boiling water. Leave it for 30 seconds, more or less, until the skin is loosened. Set the tomato in a bowl to cool. Continue with the remaining tomatoes. Add the flour to the onion mixture. Stir until the flour is mixed in and coated with oil. Continue to cook for approximate 3 minutes, stirring occasionally. Add 1 cup of the chicken stock, and stir to create a smooth sauce. Gradually mix in the remaining chicken stock and bring to a simmer over low heat. Remove the skins from the tomatoes. Also remove any stem or core. Chop the tomatoes into 1-inch chunks. Add the tomatoes to the soup. Simmer gently for 15 minutes. Stir in the cream and basil. Heat for about 2 minutes, but do not let the soup boil. Set up the food processor or blender. Using a slotted spoon, add the solids from the soup to the blender. Process briefly, then add the rest of the soup. Blend until smooth. Return the soup to the pot. Check the salt; you may not need to add any salt, depending on the saltiness of your chicken stock.</p></TEXT>

servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT></TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Jessica wanted tomato soup and we had several pounds of fresh tomatoes.  So this is what we came up with and it was very, very good.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>KaddoBourani</TEXT>
categories : [ "vegetables" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 300°F. Cut the pumpkin in half through the stem end, and cut out the long stringy fibers. Cut each pumpkin half into 3- to 4-inch pieces. There should be about 8 pieces from each pumpkin. Using a vegetable peeler, pare the rind from the pumpkins, digging the peeler down a little to remove more than just the superficial layer of rind.</p>
<p>Place the pumpkin pieces hollow sides up in a baking pan large enough to hold them in a single layer. Coat both sides of the pieces, using all of the the oil. Pour all the sugar evenly over the pieces. Cover the pan.</p>
<p>Bake the pumpkins until the color turns darker orange and becomes nearly translucent, and the texture is extremely tender, about 3 hours and 15 minutes. Baste the pieces once with the pan juices after 2 ½ hours of baking.</p>
<p>Meat Sauce: Heat the oil in a heavy, medium-sized saucepan until it ripples. Add the onions and sauté over medium-high heat, stirring frequently, until they are golden brown, about 18 minutes.</p>
<p>Add the beef and sauté, stirring constantly to break it up into tiny pieces, until the meat is no longer pink, about 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir in the tomato, garlic, coriander, salt, pepper and turmeric. Cook for 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Blend in the tomato paste. Add the water and bring to a boil over high heat. Cover, reduce heat and simmer for 15 minutes.</p>
<p>Yields 2½ cups sauce, which should be more than enough.</p>
<p>Yogurt Sauce: Stir together the yogurt, garlic, mint and salt. Cover and refrigerate until serving time. Just before serving, taste and add more salt if necessary. Yields 1 cup sauce.</p></TEXT>

time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Asakusa Nori, or just Nori, is a kind of seaweed that comes in sheets and is used for sushi rolls. Wasabi is the green Japanese horseradish.  You can buy it in a powder and reconstitute it, but try to get the wasabi that comes in a tube. To accompany this, it is nice to have some picked ginger slices, if you can find them. They normally come in a jar, and I've never seen them except in Asian markets. Pickled ginger used to always be a light pink color, but now all I see is white - I wonder if it used to contain food coloring.</p>
<p>The Japanese use a sudare mat to make sushi rolls.  It is a small flexible bamboo mat that costs about a dollar.  You can use a clean dish towel if you don't have one, but the sudare mat is much easier to use.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>Kaye'sCheeseSoup</TEXT>
categories : [ "cheeseandeggs", "soups" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In a soup pot, sauté white onion in 1 tablespoon butter or margarine for 5 minutes. Add carrots, celery, broccoli stems and garlic; sauté for 2 minutes more. Add water and bring to a boil. Cover and turn heat to medium-low; simmer for 5 minutes.</p>

id : <TEXT>Kimchi</TEXT>
categories : [ "basics" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Chop the cabbage into large pieces – don’t try to shred it or chop it too fine; ribbons about 3/8” work as well. Everything shrinks down during fermentation.</p>
<p>Make the brine of ¼ cup of salt to 4 cups of water. Place the cabbage, carrots and daikon into a large bowl or glass jar and pour in the brine. Using your fist, press on the vegetables until the liquid level rises to the top of the vegetables. The level may not rise sufficiently at first, but after an hour or so, with a few rounds of pressure on the vegetables, the liquid should cover them.</p>
<p>Weight the vegetables to keep them submerged. The liquid level will rise as the salt and pressure leaches excess liquid from the vegetables. Soak for at least 2 hours or let it sit overnight. Drain the vegetables.</p>
<p>Separately, finely dice the ginger and garlic. Add the hot pepper powder and mix well. Mix the paste into the drained vegetables. Mix in the fish sauce and salted shrimp, if you are using them. Place the mix in your fermentation vessel. Place a weight directly onto the ingredients. Press the liquid from the vegetables until it rises to cover them.  It may take several hours to draw out the natural liquids. The vegetables must remain submerged because the kimchi needs an anaerobic environment for the fermentation to take place. Keeping the vegetables from being exposed to the air also helps to prevent mold.</p>
<p>Cover with a loose fitting lid and wait 3 to14 days, more or less; 7 days is common. Watch out, as kimchi tends to bubble a lot during early fermentation; put a plate underneath the jar to catch overflow. Place in the refrigerator when the kimchi reaches your desired taste, but it will continue to slowly ferment in the refrigerator.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>lbs.</td><td>napa cabbage</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>medium</td><td>carrots, cut thin</td></tr> <tr><td>8</td><td>ounces</td><td>daikon radish, cut thin</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>cloves</td><td>garlic</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>fresh ginger, minced</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>Korean red pepper powder</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>fish sauce</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>Korean salted shrimp, minced</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Brine</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sea salt</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>cups</td><td>water, non-chlorinated</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Kimchi</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Keep tasting it after 3 days and watch how the flavors mellow and the brightness/aliveness picks up. If the room in which the fermentation takes place is cool, the fermentation process will be slower, but 3 days to a week is the normal fermentation time. You can ferment this kimchi for 3-5 weeks; it will continue to get more sour over time. Koreans are known to ferment their kimchi in a crock partially buried in the cool ground for several months, so there are many approaches.</p>
<p>The carrots are optional. Cut the daikon and the carrots very thinly, about 1/16” x 3/8”. You can cut them in strips or matchsticks, but you need them to be thin so that they will ferment in the same length of time as the cabbage.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>16</TEXT>
source : <TEXT></TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Yes, I make my own kimchi. When I started making sauerkraut, Steve said “why don’t you ever make kimchi for me?” So I did. The biggest problem is that we cannot possibly eat a giant jar of kimchi before it becomes “old.” And while you can use old kimchi in stir-fry, it loses its texture. So I make a small amount, especially compared to Korean households. Kimchi is good for your digestion and homemade is the best. Use a fermentation rig to make your kimchi, but avoid plastic as much as possible - the flavor of kimchi will permeate the plastic and the odor is impossible to remove.</p>
<p>This recipe is modified from the one at fermentationrecipes.com. The site owner is a vegetarian, so his recipe does not include the optional fish sauce or dried shrimp. I don’t use them either, but they make the recipe more authentic. If you are looking for these ingredients, kochukaru is the name of the Korean red pepper powder; it comes in large resealable bags in Asian markets. There are a variety of grinds and spiciness. Korean fermented salted shrimp are called saeujeot, and you can find the jars in the refrigerator case.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>1 quart</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>LambertsCafeThrowedRolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine teaspoon of sugar and the yeast in the tepid water. Let stand 5 to 10 minutes, until the yeast begins to foam.</p>
<p>Thoroughly mix wet ingredients in a large bowl: milk, butter, sugar, egg, and salt. Stir in yeast mixture.</p>
<p>Stir in 3 ½ cups of flour, adding a bit more if necessary to make a soft, pliable dough.</p>
<p>Turn dough out onto a floured surface and let rest for 5 minutes. While the dough is resting, clean and butter the bowl.</p>
<p>Knead dough in the stand mixer for 5 minutes, adding flour if necessary, until the dough is smooth and silky. It may take longer if you knead by hand.</p>
<p>Return dough to bowl, cover with plastic wrap, and let rise in a warm place until doubled in size.</p>
<p>Lightly butter muffin cups or muffin tin. Punch down dough.</p>
<p>Cut dough into 24 pieces with your sharpest knife. Roll dough pieces into smooth balls. Place two balls in each muffin cup. It should be a tight fit.</p>
<p>Cover tins loosely with plastic wrap for 45 minutes. Preheat oven to 350°F during last 15 minutes of rising.</p>
<p>Bake rolls for 20 minutes or until light brown. They should be 190°Fat the center. Remove from muffin wraps as soon as they are cool enough to do so without doing permanent damage. Throw. </p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>LemonMeringuePie</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Pre-bake pie shell if needed. Let cool completely before continuing.</p>
<p>Position a rack in the middle of the oven. Preheat the oven to 375°F.</p>
<p>Place the egg whites and create of tartar in the bowl of a stand mixer that is fitted with the whisk attachment. Set aside.</p>
<p>Whisk the egg yolks in a medium bowl (not a small bowl). Set aside.</p>
<p>Whisk together the cornstarch, 1½ cups sugar and salt in a medium saucepan. Add water, butter, lemon juice and lemon zest. Bring the mixture to a simmer over medium heat, whisking gently. Be patient and do not boil the mixture. Alton does not provide any test for doneness here, but many recipes say that the mixture should "coat the back of a spoon."  Remove the pot from the heat.</p>
<p>One whisk-full at a time, add the lemon mixture to the egg yolks and stir until incorporated. Do this until the eggs are warm and the mixture looks more like custard than yolks, then whisk it back into the pot. Over low heat, stir the mixture from 1 minute, then pour into pie crust.</p>
<p>Make the meringue: Beat the egg whites until soft peaks form. Then add sugar gradually while beating until stiff peaks form, about 2 minutes. Top the pie with meringue immediately - the filling should be hot. Be certain to seal in the filling completely, especially at the edge of the crust.</p>
<p>Bake for 10 to 12 minutes, until the meringue is golden brown. Remove from the oven and cool on a rack.</p>
<p>DO NOT CUT the pie until it is completely cool - about 6 hours. Premature cutting will break the starch matrix and turn the filling to lemon soup.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>LemonMeringueTartlets</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies", "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Arrange the cooled pastry shells on two large baking sheets (with raised edges).</p>
<p>Lemon Curd: Combine the egg, egg yolks and sugar in a 1½ quart heavy saucepan. Stir in the lemon juice and zest. Cook over medium-low heat for 2-3 minutes, stirring occasionally,  until the mixture thickens to a hollandaise sauce consistency. Pour into a bowl and cover the surface of the lemon curd with plastic. Refrigerate until chilled (or for up to 3 days).</p>

Using an electric mixer, preferably with a whisk attachment, whip until the mixture has peaks that are thick and shiny, about 10 to 15 minutes. Attach a ¼ inch open star decorating tip to a pastry bag. Fill bag with meringue and pipe a tall swirl on each tartlet. Bake for 3 to 4 minutes, until the meringue is light golden. Place baking sheet on a wire rack until tartlets are cool. (It is natural for the meringue to deflate slightly during cooling.)</p>
<p>Serve the same day.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>LemonPoppySeedPoundCake</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>All ingredients (even the eggs) must be at room temperature. Preheat oven to 350°F.</p>
<p>Prepare the pan by greasing and then flouring it. If using a loaf pan, grease the pan and line the bottom of the pan with parchment paper; then flour it.</p>
<p>In a medium bowl, lightly combine the milk, eggs, and vanilla.</p>
<p>In a large mixing bowl (or the bowl of a stand mixer), combine the dry ingredients, including the poppy seeds and lemon zest. Mix on low speed for 30 seconds to blend.</p>
<p>Add the butter and half the egg mixture. Mix on low speed until ingredients are moistened. Increase to high speed (medium on a stand mixer) and beat for 1 minute to aerate and develop the cake’s structure.</p>
<p>Scrape down the sides of the bowl. Gradually add the remaining egg mixture in two batches, beating for 20 seconds after each addition to incorporate the ingredients and strengthen the structure. Scrape down the sides.</p>
<p>Scrape batter into the pan and smooth the top with a spatula. The batter will be almost ½ inch from the top of the 4-cup loaf pan. (If your pan is smaller, use any excess batter for cupcakes.)</p>
<p>Bake 55 to 65 minutes or until a wooden toothpick inserted in the center comes out clean. To get an attractive split down the middle, wait until the cake has baked for 20 minutes and then, with a lightly-greased sharp knife, make a shallow mark down the middle of the cake.</p>
<p>Cover loosely with buttered foil after 30 minutes to prevent over-browning. The cake should not shrink from the sides of the pan while it is in the oven.</p>
<p>Let the cake cook in the pan on a rack for 10 minutes. Invert onto a greased rack, then re-invert. Cool completely before wrapping tight.</p>
<p>Lemon Syrup: The lemon syrup adds additional flavor and moisture. It also keeps the cake fresh for a few days longer. But I still usually omit it. Shortly before the cake is done, prepare the lemon syrup. In a small pan over medium heat, combine the sugar and lemon juice until sugar dissolves. As soon as the cake comes out of the oven, poke the cake all over with a toothpick or wire tester; brush with ½ of the syrup. When the cake is inverted and removed from the pan, repeat the poking and brush with more of the syrup. Re-invert the cake and brush the sides with the remaining syrup.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>milk</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>large</td><td>eggs</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>vanilla</td></tr> <tr><td>150</td><td>grams</td><td>cake flour, sifted (1 ½ cups)</td></tr> <tr><td>150</td><td>grams</td><td>sugar, (3/4 cup)</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>28</td><td>grams</td><td>poppy seeds, (3 Tbsp.)</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>lemon zest, finely grated</td></tr> <tr><td>184</td><td>grams</td><td>unsalted butter, softened (13 Tbsp.)</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Lemon Syrup</td></tr> <tr><td>75</td><td>grams</td><td>sugar, (6 Tbsp.)</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>fresh lemon juice</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Lemon Poppy Seed Pound Cake</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>This is a variation on Ruth’s “Perfect Pound Cake.” To make the original version, omit the poppy seeds and lemon peel; do not use the lemon syrup.</p>
<p>Another excellent variation is “Double-Vanilla Pound Cake.” Omit the poppy seeds, lemon peel, and lemon syrup. Using a small sharp knife, split a vanilla bean; if you have a Tahitian vanilla bean that is very aromatic, you may only need ½ of the bean. Put the split bean into a small saucepan with the milk and scald it. Cover immediately, and let cool to room temperature. Remove the vanilla bean and scrape the seeds back into the milk. Add the vanilla-infused milk to the eggs and vanilla extract. Proceed as usual.</p>
<p>You can make this cake in a 6-cup fluted tube pan, if you prefer. The recipe is best in a 4-cup loaf pan, but can be made in a 6-cup loaf pan instead.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The Cake Bible, Rose Levy Beranbaum</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Ruth Levy Beranbaum is a genius when it comes to cake. She does meticulous research and testing, and it shows in every one of her cake recipes. Try the variations to this recipe, too.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>LisasAddictiveCookies</TEXT>
categories : [ "cookiesandbars" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 350°.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, cream butter and confectioners' sugar until light and fluffy. Beat in extract and Fiori di Sicilia. Combine flour, cornstarch and lemon juice powder; gradually add to creamed mixture and mix well.</p>
<p>Shape into 1-inch balls. Place 2 inches apart on un-greased baking sheets. Bake 10-12 minutes or until bottoms are lightly browned. Remove from oven and let sit for a minute or two on the cookie sheet. Then remove cookies to wire racks to cool.</p>

<p>Cookies: Replace lemon extract with peppermint extract. Omit Fiori di Sicilia and lemon juice powder.</p>
<p>Frosting: Replace lemon extract with peppermint extract; omit lemon oil. Use 2 drops of red food coloring instead of yellow, or omit food coloring. After frosting, sprinkle the cookies with ½ cup finely crushed peppermint candies.</p></TEXT>

time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Well, I finally bought a bread machine a couple of years ago and the Zojirushi is a wonderful device. It can do a ton of stuff besides just bake bread, but this is the main reason that I use it. It turns out a lovely and consistent loaf every time. I think this is technically a 1½-lb. loaf, but it seems larger.</p>
<p>I have tweaked this bread recipe for a couple of years now. It makes a high-rising loaf that will make sandwiches or toast. The bread has great flavor as well. Because this recipe has eggs and dairy, you cannot use any time delay features. You can vary the ratio of the flours; this ratio gives a light loaf that Steve will occasionally actually eat. I prefer to use King Arthur Flour’s Irish-style whole wheat flour as it makes a delicious bread. If I don’t have that, a sprouted whole-wheat flour also works well. But any good whole wheat flour will do. For the white flour, bread flour is best, but again, all-purpose flour will work too. Just avoid cake flour or pastry flour.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>MarescaFamilyChickenCacciatore</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Rinse chicken and pat dry. Mix flour, ½ teaspoon salt and ¼ teaspoon pepper. Dredge chicken in flour and set aside. introduction : <TEXT><p>Joe Rath got this recipe from the old Island X restaurant in Little Rock; that place has been closed since the 1970s. I used to put some chicken breasts and this marinade in a plastic freezer bag, and stick it in the ice chest for camping trips. After a day or two, we would grill the chicken over the campfire. Top it off with some caramelized red onions for flavor and garnish. Yum. If you have some fried plantains on the side, you've got a traditional Cuban dinner.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>MeltinYourMouthRolls</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Beat butter and sugar until fluffy. Beat in eggs.</p>
<p>Dissolve yeast in ½ cup warm water with a dash of sugar. Add yeast, 1¾ cup water, and 2 tsp. salt to creamed mixture.</p>
<p>Stir in enough flour to make a soft, sticky dough. Cover and let dough rise in the bowl for 3 hours in refrigerator.</p>
<p>Place dough on well-floured board and pat out flat. Spread dough with soft butter -- the butter must be at room temperature and very soft.</p>
<p>Fold dough and pat out again. Cut into rolls with a cookie cutter. Place rolls in well-greased pans or muffin tins. Let rise 2 hours.</p>
<p>Bake at 425°Ffor 12 minutes (or more); the rolls need to be nice and brown.</p>
<p>Reheat at 325°F.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>MiniatureTartletPastry</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies", "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Put the flour, salt and sugar in a food processor bowl. Process just to blend the ingredients. Scatter all the butter slices over the flour mixture. Process with on/off bursts until the mixture has the consistency of cornmeal.</p>
<p>Whisk the egg and vanilla together in a small bowl. With the food processor running, pour the egg mixture down the feed tube. Process until the ingredients form a ball. Remove the dough to a work surface.</p>
<p>Using the heel of your hand, press dough together until it is smooth and cohesive.</p>
<p>Adjust rack to lower third of oven and preheat oven to 350°F.</p>
<p>Arrange 4 dozen tartlet tins close together on 12x15 baking sheets with a rim. Pinch off 1 teaspoon of dough at a time and drop it into a tin. Drop a piece of dough into every tin. Then take each tin and remove the dough - roll it into a ball in the palm of your hands.  (This helps shape the dough more evenly.) Drop the ball into the tin, and press the center of the dough into the bottom of the tin with your index finger. Then press dough up on the sides of the tin, while rotating the tin. The goal is to use just enough dough to line the tin, without creating a thick shell. If you have help, set this up as an assembly line.</p>
<p>Bake tartlet shells for 12 to 15 minutes, or until light golden. Remove from baking sheet (but leave in tins) to cool. When the tins are cool enough to touch, squeeze each tin lightly between your thumb and forefinger. Turn the tin upside down and let the shell drop into the palm of your other hand. Repeat until all dough is cooked.</p>
<p>Stack cool, unfilled shells in an airtight container and store at room temperature for up to a week. You can also refrigerate the uncooked dough (well wrapped) for up to a week, or freeze it for up to a month. Bring dough to room temperature before working with it.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>unsifted flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1/8</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/3</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>8</td><td>ounces</td><td>unsalted butter, cut in ¼-inch slices</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "gluten-free" ]
title : <TEXT>Miniature Tartlet Pastry</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>For a gluten-free variation: Use gluten-free flour, and add 1 teaspoon of xanthan gum powder.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>48</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Sweet Minatures</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I started making miniature desserts for Wolf and Cheryl's annual Thanksgiving dinner.  When you have a dozen different desserts, you can't try them all - unless they are miniatures! They tasted great, and everyone loved the fact that they could just have a taste.</p>
<p>This pastry is more like a cookie dough, which is perfect for miniatures. With a high proportion of dough to filling, the dough should offer some flavor, too. To make these, you will need to invest in some miniature tartlet tins. Flo Baker recommends the 1.5-inch fluted tin, and that has worked well for me. You might have to go to a cooking supply store to get these, but it's worth it.  If you don't want to spend all night cooking the shells, then get at least 2 dozen tins. Flo Baker recommends 4 dozen!  Also, plan to make the pastry a few days (or a week) before you need it; it will be easier on you.</p>
<p>My favorite filling for this is the Lemon Meringue Tartlet recipe. I have also filled these shells with Nutella (a big hit), and canned cherry pie filling.  But you can fill these with almost anything sweet!</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>8 dozen</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>MiracleNoKneadBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In a large mixing bowl, whisk the flour, salt and yeast together. Stir in water until chunky, thick dough forms. If it needs a little more water, add a few more teaspoons until dough is scrappy and sticky.</p>
<p>Cover mixing bowl with plastic wrap and let it rest for 12-18 hours at room temperature.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 450°F. Place a 6 quart dutch oven in for 30 minutes to heat.</p>
<p>Gently scrape dough (should be risen and covered with little bubbles) onto a well floured surface. Gently shape into a ball with flour on the outside and place on a piece of parchment and cover with plastic film while the pan heats.</p>
<p>Remove the plastic, lift the dough and parchment together into the pan and bake covered for 30 minutes. Remove the cover and bake another 10-15 minutes to brown and crisp the crust!</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>MurghRasedarChickeninFriedOnionSauce</TEXT>
categories : [ "chicken", "indian" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Chop 2 onions coarsely. Cut the remaining onions in half lengthwise, and slice thinly crosswise.</p>
<p>Put chopped onions, ginger and garlic in a blender and process until you have a paste. Set aside.</p>
<p>Heat oil in a large pot over medium heat. Add sliced onions; stir and fry until they are a deep reddish-brown, about 20 minutes. Remove onions, leaving behind as much oil as possible.</p>
<p>Set aside to drain on paper towels. Remove pan from heat. Avert your face, and add paste to pan. Put pan back over heat; stir and fry until paste is brown, about 4 minutes. Add coriander, cumin, turmeric and cayenne; stir once.</p>

<p>Cover, turn heat to low, and cook for 20 minutes. Add garam masala and the sautéed onions; mix. Cook, uncovered, on medium heat for about 8 minutes until the sauce reduces and thickens. Skim any fat. Place chicken in a warm serving dish and sprinkle with the cilantro.</p></TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Sauté the mushrooms and onions in 1 tablespoon of the butter and 1 tablespoon oil until they are browned, about 5 minutes. Sprinkle in the tablespoon of flour; stir over low heat for 1 minute to coat the vegetables and to remove the raw flour taste.</p>
<p>Add ¼ cup milk and stir until thick. Stir in ¼ teaspoon salt and set aside.</p>
<p>Place the ½ cup flour in a 2-qt. pan; beat in 2 cups milk with a wire whisk. Place over medium heat and stir constantly until the mixture thickens and boils. Remove from heat; stir in the remaining 3 Tbsp. butter, the seasonings, and the eggs - one by one. Finally, stir in 1 cup of cheese.</p>
<p>Place ½ of the mixture in a well-oiled casserole. Spread mushroom mixture gently over top. Pour the remainder of the eggs over the top. Sprinkle with the remaining cheese. Bake in a preheated oven at 400°F. for 25 minutes. Use a rack positioned in the upper ⅓ of the oven.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>OatmealBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine oats, salt, molasses and shortening in a large bowl. Pour in boiling water and stir until just mixed. Let stand until cool. Mix yeast with 1/3 cup warm water until dissolved. Add to oatmeal mixture and stir well. Add 2 cups of flour and stir for 3 minutes, until a smooth and elastic batter is formed. Add remaining flour, 1 cup at a time. Reserve the last ½ cup flour for kneading if you can.</p>
<p>Turn out dough on floured surface and knead gently for 3 to 4 minutes. Dough should be soft, but not too sticky. Place dough in a lightly oiled bowl and turn to coat. Cover and let rise until doubled, about 1 hour or more.</p>
<p>Work dough down and divide in half. Shape into loaves and place in greased loaf pans. Let rise again until doubled, about 45 minutes to 1 hour.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°F. Bake loaves for 45 minutes or until done. Remove from pans and let stand for 10 minutes before cutting.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>quick cooking oats, heaping</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>molasses</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>boiling water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>package</td><td>yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1/3</td><td>cup</td><td>warm water</td></tr> <tr><td>5 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>flour</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Oatmeal Bread</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Sulphured molasses or blackstrap molasses will taste very strong; use unsulphured. The recipe also says not to use the quick rising type of yeast; I don't know why.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>24</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Mrs. A. E. Purvis</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This recipe is from the Purvis' grandmother; I got the recipe from Toodie. I had this bread one year at Christmas and it was great.</p>
<p>Although this bread is very dark brown, it is lighter than most dark breads since it uses regular flour.  It is also pretty sweet because of the molasses.  The smell is amazing when it is cooking!</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>OatmealRaisinBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In a large bowl, mix together 3 cups of the flour, dry milk, gluten, and brown sugar.</p>
<p>Cook oats in 4 cups water until soft (5 to 10 minutes). Stir in honey and salt; let cool to lukewarm. Dissolve yeast in ½ cup of warm water.</p>
<p>To the bowl, add the oat mixture and the yeast mixture. Beat until smooth. Let this sponge rise until double, about 1 hour. (Do not let sponge over-rise!)</p>
<p>Stir the sponge down. Add the raisins, cinnamon, egg, butter, and remaining 3 cups whole wheat flour. Sprinkle 1 cup of white flour onto work surface, and turn the dough out onto it. Knead about 10 minutes, adding the second cup of white flour as needed. Let dough rise until doubled, about 1 hour.</p>
<p>Punch dough down and shape into 4 loaves. At this point, you may roll out each loaf and spread it with butter, cinnamon and sugar; roll up as for a jelly roll. Seal ends and seams. Place loaves seam side down in a greased baking pan.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°F.  Allow loaves to rise for about ½ hour. Bake loaves for approximately 45 minutes.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>OrangeFlavoredChicken</TEXT>
categories : [ "chicken" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Prepare the oranges: Cut 8 strips of peel, each about 2 inches long by ½ inch wide. Zest orange until you have 1½ teaspoon of fine zest. Juice the oranges to obtain ¾ cup orange juice. You may need only 2 of the oranges, depending on their size.</p>
<p>Marinade: Combine all marinade ingredients - except orange peel strips - in a large saucepan until sugar is fully dissolved. Transfer ¾ cup of the mixture to a medium bowl and add the chicken. Let marinate for at least 10 minutes, or up to an hour.</p>
<p>In a small bowl, mix cornstarch and water. Bring the mixture in the saucepan to simmer over high heat. Whisk the cornstarch slurry into the sauce, then bring it to a simmer. Cook, stirring occasionally, until thick and translucent, about 1 minute. Off the heat, stir in the orange peel strips and the dried peppers. The sauce should measure about 1½ cups.</p>
<p>For the coating: Using a fork, lightly beat the egg whites in a shallow dish until frothy. In a second shallow dish, whisk cornstarch, baking soda and cayenne until mixed. Drain the chicken and pat dry with paper towels. In batches, coat the chicken with the egg mixture; then transfer to the cornstarch mixture and dredge gently. Gently shake off excess and place chicken pieces on a wire rack to dry slightly. Repeat with remaining chicken.</p>
<p>Fry the chicken: Heat 3 cups oil in a Dutch oven over high heat until the oil registers 350°F. Carefully place half the chicken in the oil and fry until golden-brown, about 5 minutes. Turn each piece with tongs, about halfway through. Transfer the cooked chicken to a paper towel-lined plate. Repeat with the remaining chicken pieces.</p>
<p>To serve, reheat the sauce over medium heat until simmering, about 2 minutes. Add the fried chicken and gently toss to coat. Serve when heated through.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Marinade and Sauce</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cup</td><td>low-sodium chicken broth</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td></td><td>oranges</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>dark brown sugar, packed</td></tr> <tr><td>6</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>distilled vinegar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>soy sauce</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>garlic, minced</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>fresh ginger, grated</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cayenne</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>lbs.</td><td>boned and skinned chicken thighs, cut in 1½" pieces</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>cold water</td></tr> <tr><td>5</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>cornstarch</td></tr> <tr><td>8</td><td>small</td><td>dried red chiles, optional</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Coating</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>large</td><td>egg whites</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>cornstarch</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>baking soda</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cayenne</td></tr></table></TEXT>

servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Spread the cream cheese over each half of the loaf. Spread most of olives over bottom half of loaf, then layer on the sliced tomatoes, overlapping them. Salt lightly. title : <TEXT>Pan Bagnia (Sandwich)</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Use a long loaf of French bread.  The recipe calls for either watercress or arugula; you will need only a small bunch.  You will need 2 to 3 red bell peppers to yield 1 cup of thin slices.  Be sure to use a fresh, sweet onion.  I prefer purple onion, or sometimes sliced green onion.   Use enough cream cheese to keep the bread from getting soggy, or more if you like the flavor it adds. You may use any other type of cheese you like, or none at all.  Provolone, Mozzarella, and Parmesan are all good choices.  If using cheese, slice it thinly.</p>
<p>Other optional ingredients include: sliced hard-boiled eggs, capers, roasted red peppers, anchovies, 1 cup artichoke hearts cut in quarters, ½ cup pesto and herbs such as basil, marjoram, oregano or thyme.</p>
<p>You can press the sandwich by weighting it with a large book or a baking tray topped with bricks. Press for at least an hour.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>New Vegetarian Epicure</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I don't really like sandwiches much, but I do like this sandwich.  I usually make a single serving (one sandwich), though.  One of the things I like about this is that it gets better by standing, instead of soggy like most sandwiches.  When I'm being organized, I sometimes make one of these to take sailing.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>Pavlova</TEXT>
categories : [ "desserts", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 250°F.</p>
<p>Draw a 9-inch circle on a sheet of parchment paper and place it on a large cookie sheet.</p>
<p>In a large mixing bowl, beat egg whites with cream of tartar until foamy, using low speed of mixer. Increase speed to high and beat until soft peaks form. Beat in sugar, 1 tablespoon at a time.  Beat 10 seconds after each addition to be sure the sugar dissolves. Beat in lemon juice. Whites should be stiff, dense and glossy.</p>
<p>Sprinkle ½ cup of confectioner’s sugar over the egg whites. With a spatula, gently fold in until blended. (I used the low speed of the mixer, quickly, and it worked okay.)</p>
<p>Spread meringue into the parchment circle, 1½ inch high on the edge, and 1 inch in the center. Bake in the middle of the oven for 1 hour.</p>
<p>Reduce heat to 200°Fand bake for 1 more hour.</p>
<p>Turn off the oven, leave the door shut, and let the meringue rest for 1½ hours or overnight.</p>
<p>Peel the paper from the meringue carefully and place the meringue on a serving platter.</p>
<p>In a large bowl, beat the cream with 1 tablespoon confectioner’s sugar and vanilla extract until stiff peaks form.</p>
<p>Spread about half the cream in the meringue shell and cover with the strawberries. Overlap kiwi slices around the inner rim and garnish with mint. Reserve the remaining whipped cream to serve with the pavlova.</p>
<p>Note that the cream will gradually absorb into the meringue and soften it, so assemble the dessert within an hour of serving it for best results.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>6</td><td></td><td>egg whites, at room temperature</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cream of tartar</td></tr> <tr><td>1 1/3</td><td>cups</td><td>sugar, superfine</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>lemon juice</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>confectioner's sugar, sifted</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>heavy cream, chilled</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>confectioner's sugar, sifted</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>cups</td><td>strawberries, (2 pints) thinly sliced</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td></td><td>kiwi fruit, peeled and sliced</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>fresh mint sprigs, for garnish</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Pavlova</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You can substitute any fruit you like for the topping. The original recipe called for a mix of kiwi, pineapple and raspberries; it also used twice as much whipped cream.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>8</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Food and Wine Magazine</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is a great presentation dessert and good for special occasions. It is best if the meringue is made the night before.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>PizzaDough</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>In a large mixing bowl, combine ingredients with a fork.</p>
<p>Once the dough begins to come together, scrape out onto a lightly floured work surface. Knead until soft and smooth, 5 to 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Place dough in a clean mixing bowl and cover with plastic wrap. Allow to rise, about 2 hours, until doubled.</p>
<p>Divide dough into two parts. Lightly oil each piece and place it in a plastic bag. Place the bags in the refrigerator (or freeze). Use refrigerated dough within 3 days.</p>
<p>On the day you want to cook, remove the dough from the refrigerator at least an hour before cooking. For frozen dough, move it from the freezer to the refrigerator the night before.</p>
<p>If you are using a pizza stone, position it in the oven. Preheat oven to 450°F(or higher) for at least 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Working on a floured surface, press and stretch each dough ball to form a round. Work from the center to the edge. Use a rolling pin if necessary. If the dough is very elastic, allow it to rest for 5 minutes and then try again.</p>
<p>I cut circles of parchment paper for making pizza. The circles give me a target size for shaping the dough, but they also make it simple to move the pizzas around. After placing the pizza in the oven, wait about 3-5 minutes, then jerk the paper from beneath the pizza. You may be able to reuse the paper for a second pizza. (I usually make 2 to 10 pizzas in a session, with each person topping their own pizza.)</p>
<p>When dough is shaped, add toppings, leaving a 1-inch border around the edge.</p>
<p>Bake until edges are golden and cheese is bubbling, 10-15 minutes. The bottom of the crust should be crisp and brown, with occasional darker patches.</p>
<p>Makes two 10-inch pizza crusts, or 4 smaller pizzas.  Recipe can be doubled.</p>
<p>My Personal Topping Ratios for a 10-inch pizza:</p>
<p>½ cup sauce or less</p>
<p>4 oz meat (about 1 cup or less)</p>
<p>1 cup vegetables (onion, olives, bell pepper, whatever you like)</p>
<p>1½ cups grated cheese</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>500</td><td>grams</td><td>flour, (4 cups)</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>cups</td><td>lukewarm water, (300 grams)</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>olive oil, optional</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "pizza" ]
title : <TEXT>Pizza Dough</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>2</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>DeLallo Flour Bag: Pizza alla Napoletana Doug</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Over the years, I’ve made a lot of home-made pizza. I’ve tried all kinds of flour and techniques. While there is no single answer, this is my preference for home-made pizza. I use 100% Italian Tipo “00” flour - you can find it in a lot of grocery stores these days. My preferred brand is DeLallo Organic; DeLallo also makes a nice pizza sauce. I don’t use any oil in the dough. Keeping the dough in the refrigerator overnight really develops its character, but if you must use it on the same day, you can. Just skip the refrigeration step.</p>
<p>Another thing that will improve home-made pizza is more heat. Usually that comes from a pizza stone. I have two: one is a traditional stone; the other is a slab of stainless steel that I bought from a company called “Baking Steel.” The steel weighs a ton, but it works great. Finally, I broke down and bought a Breville Crispy Crust Pizza Maker, and it is awesome too.</p>
<p>Whatever you do, preheat the oven and the stone a lot. That means at least a half hour of preheating for a regular oven.</p>
<p>You may also want to experiment with setting the heat even higher; wood-fired pizza ovens typically cook at 800°F. I set the countertop Breville to its maximum of 660°F.</p>
<p>Finally, Italians don’t overload their pizzas and neither should you. Use a few high quality ingredients and let the taste of the crust come through. Piling on the toppings will slow the cooking and prevent the crust from becoming crisp. The toppings should all be warm or room-temperature when you put them on the pizza.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>
---
id : <TEXT>PizzaNapoletana</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Stir together flour, salt and yeast in a 4-quart bowl.  With a large metal spoon, stir in the oil and the cold water until all of the flour is absorbed.  (Or mix on low speed of stand mixer.)</p>
<p>Now, if you are mixing by hand, repeatedly dip your hand or the metal spoon into cold water and use it like a dough hook to work the dough vigorously into a smooth mass.  Rotate the bowl while you do this.  Do this for 5 to 7 minutes, or as long as it takes to develop smooth sticky dough.</p>
<p>If you are using a mixer, switch to the dough hook and mix on medium until you get a smooth sticky dough.  The dough should clear the sides of the bowl, but stick to the bottom.  The finished dough will be springy, elastic and sticky - not just tacky - with a temperature of 50° - 55°F.</p>
<p>Prepare a sheet pan by lining it with parchment and then lightly oiling (or spraying) the parchment.  Sprinkle flour on the counter and turn out the dough.  Separate the dough into 6 equal parts.  Sprinkle flour over the dough and flour your dry hands.  Lift each piece of dough and gently round it into a ball.  Place the dough balls on the sheet pan.  Spray the dough generously with oil and slip the pan into a food-grade plastic bag. Refrigerate for up to 3 days.</p>
<p>On the day that you plan to make the pizza, remove the dough 2 hours before you plan to cook it.  Dust the counter will flour, and mist with spray oil.  Place the dough balls on the counter and sprinkle them with flour; dust your hands with flour..  Press each ball into a disk about 5" across and 1/2" thick.  Cover the dough loosely with plastic.  Let rest for 2 hours.</p>
<p>At least 45 minutes before making, place a baking stone on a rack in the lower third of the oven. Preheat the oven as high as it will go, about 550°F.</p>
<p>Shape the dough. If it refuses to stretch, let it rest for 5 to 20 minutes. Each 6-oz piece of dough should stretch to 9 to 12 inches in diameter. Top the pizza and then slide into the oven. After 2 minutes, check the pizza and rotate it 180 degrees for even baking. It should be done in 3-6 minutes longer. Wait 3-5 minutes before slicing.</p>
<p>On the day that you plan to make the pizza, remove the dough 2 hours before you plan to cook it.  Dust the counter will flour, and mist with spray oil.  Place the dough balls on the counter and sprinkle them with flour; dust your hands with flour..  Press each ball into a disk about 5" across and 1/2" thick.  Cover the dough loosely with plastic.  Let rest for 2 hours.</p>
<p>At least 45 minutes before making, place a baking stone on a rack in the lower third of the oven. Preheat the oven as high as it will go, about 550°F.</p>
<p>Shape the dough. If it refuses to stretch, let it rest for 5 to 20 minutes. Each 6-oz piece of dough should stretch to 9 to 12 inches in diameter. Top the pizza and then slide into the oven.</p>
<p>After 2 minutes, check the pizza and rotate it 180 degrees for even baking. It should be done in 3-6 minutes longer. Wait 3-5 minutes before slicing.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>20 ¼</td><td>ounces</td><td>unbleached flour, (4 ½ cups)</td></tr> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>instant yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>olive oil</td></tr> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>water, (ice cold, 40°F)</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Pizza Napoletana</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The Bread Baker's Apprentice</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is a very detailed and very wonderful recipe for pizza. I try to follow these directions, but I use the ingredients in the updated Pizza recipe in this collection. I think that everything that Peter Reinhart does with bread is amazing.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>6 10-inch pizzas</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>RefrigeratorRyeBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine 2 cups of unbleached flour, brown sugar, yeast, salt and orange peel in a large bowl. Mix.</p>
<p>Heat liquids and margarine until very warm (120°F). Add liquids to bowl gradually, beating with high speed of an electric mixer. Beat 3 minutes more. Stir in rye flour and enough additional white flour to make a soft dough.</p>
<p>Knead until smooth and elastic, about 5 minutes. Let dough rest for 20 minutes.</p>
<p>Divide in half. Shape dough into loaves as for French bread. Place loaves on a greased baking sheet that has been dusted with cornmeal.</p>
<p>Cover with plastic; refrigerate for 2 to 24 hours.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 400°F. Remove loaves from refrigerator and let stand for 15 minutes, uncovered. Bake for 40 minutes or until done.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>3 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>unbleached flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>brown sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>grated orange peel</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>hot water</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>molasses</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>margarine</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>cups</td><td>rye flour</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Refrigerator Rye Bread</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>This recipe asks you to shape the bread into long loaves like French bread.  Shape it any way you like, although this recipe will not make good rolls.</p>
<p>By the way, if you do like caraway seeds, you can use 1 tablespoon of caraway seeds instead of the grated orange peel.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>16</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Bread and Soup Cookbook</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>After I started baking bread, I realized that I liked rye bread - I just didn't like caraway seeds and some of the other stuff that people often put in rye bread. This bread doesn't have anything that I don't like. Rye bread is heavy, so don't expect light and airy loaves. This particular recipe should be about like whole wheat bread or maybe a little lighter, since it is half white flour.</p>
<p>If you only use rye flour occasionally, you need to store it in the refrigerator. Otherwise, the natural oils in the rye flour will spoil and give it an off taste. At this point, I buy only enough rye flour for whatever I am making, and throw away any leftover. This only works if you can buy exactly the amount you need; try a health-food store that sells staples in bulk. Smell the flour before you buy it; if it doesn't have any odor, that's okay. If it has become rancid, you will be able to tell.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>2 loaves</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>RyeBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Stir together the flours, salt, dry yeast, and caraway seeds in the bowl of the stand mixer. Add the molasses, shortening, water, and liquid caramel coloring if using.</p>
<p>Knead for 4 minutes by machine (up to 6 minutes by hand), adding sprinkles of flour if necessary. The dough should feel supple and pliable, a little tacky but not sticky. Lightly oil a large bowl and place the dough in it; roll the dough to lightly cover it with oil. Cover the bowl with plastic wrap.</p>
<p>Let rise until double, about 90 minutes.</p>
<p>Turn out onto a floured counter. Divide and shape into 2 loaves. Place each in a pan, or shape them as desired and place them on a baking sheet. Mist the dough with spray oil and cover loosely with plastic wrap. (You can hold the dough for up to 2 days in the refrigerator at this point.) Let rise for 60 to 90 minutes, or until almost doubled in size.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°F.</p>
<p>Whisk together the egg wash, and brush over the loaves evenly but gently.</p>
<p>Bak for approximately 45 minutes, depending on your oven and the shape of the loaves. The internal temperature of the bread should be 190°F, and the loaves should sound hollow when thumped on the bottom.</p>
<p>Allow loaves to cool for 2 hours before slicing or serving.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>6</td><td>ounces</td><td>rye flour, (light or medium - 1 ½ c)</td></tr> <tr><td>13.5</td><td>ounces</td><td>bread flour, (3 cups)</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>caraway seed, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>molasses</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>shortening</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>cups</td><td>water, at room temp</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>liquid caramel coloring, for dark rye bread</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Egg wash</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>water</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Rye Bread</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Use clear flour instead of bread flour, if you can get it. It is sometimes called “first clear flour.”</p>
<p>This recipe calls for optional caramel coloring. If you use it, the bread will look darker, but will be otherwise the same. If you don’t have caramel coloring, you could use 2 tablespoons of cocoa, carob, or coffee powder, mixed with 1 tablespoon of water.</p>
<p>Variation: Marbled Rye Bread - this combines a light dough with a dark dough in a spiral or other shape. It looks cool, but it tastes the same. Marbled Rye is a popular style of bread in New York delis. To prepare it: make 1 recipe of dough without the caramel coloring, and one recipe using the caramel coloring. When dividing and sharing the dough, separate each recipe into 4 pieces instead of 2. For each loaf, take one piece of white dough and one piece of dark dough. Roll the pieces together in spirals, torpedos, or however you wish. You will end up with 4 loaves of bread, since you have made 2 recipes of dough.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>20</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The Bread Baker's Apprentice</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This makes a great rye bread for sandwiches.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SantaMariaStyleTritip</TEXT>
categories : [ "beef"]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine all dry rub ingredients in a small container.</p>
<p>Remove the external fat and silver skin from the roast. Place it on a sheet of plastic wrap.</p>
<p>Generously coat the roast with about 4 tablespoons of the dry rub, coating all sides.</p>
<p>Tightly wrap the seasoned meat and refrigerate at least 3 hours. You may refrigerate for up to 3 days.</p>
<p>One hour before grilling, remove the roast from the refrigerator and let it come to room temperature.</p>
<p>Clean the grill with a paper towel dipped in vegetable oil, to prevent sticking. Heat the grill to medium-high.</p>
<p>Once the grill is very hot, sear one side of the meat for 10 minutes. Turn and repeat on the second side.</p>
<p>Turn heat to medium and close the lid of the grill. Allow the meat to cook for 15 to 25 minutes.</p>
<p>Remove the meat when the thickest part reaches about 120°F(medium rare).</p>
<p>Wrap the meat loosely in aluminum foil and let rest for at least 15 minutes before slicing. Thinly slice against the grain.</p></TEXT>
