id : <TEXT>Sauerkraut</TEXT>
categories : [ "basics" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Make sure that all the jars, bowls and your hands are very clean before you begin. You don’t want to ferment anything nasty.</p>
<p>Measure the salt into a small bowl or cup.</p>
<p>Start by removing the outer leaves from the cabbage if they are looking a little sketchy. it they look fine, you can leave them and rinse them off to remove potential contaminants. Cut the cabbage into ½” wide ribbons. I cut the cabbage in half or quarters first, depending on its size. Then I cut out the core and start slicing. You can make the ribbons into any size you like, but I find that thinner pieces don’t retain as much crunch as I like. Place the cabbage in a large bowl as you slice it, preferably made of glass. I like to sprinkle the salt over the cabbage as I go, or you can mix it in all at once.</p>
<p>After all the cabbage is sliced, toss the cabbage and the salt to mix well. I use my hands and give the cabbage a squeeze as I toss. If it feels wet, that is good. Let the cabbage sweat in the bowl for about an hour.</p>
<p>Mix in the berries and seeds if you are using them. Place everything, including any accumulated liquid, into your fermenting vessel. I use a large-mouth Mason jar that is large enough to hold it all - either a quart or half-gallon size. I squeeze the cabbage again as I add it to the jar.</p>
<p>Once you have the cabbage in the jar, press it very hard. You can use your fist, a wooden spoon or an implement made for the purpose (called a pickle press). Keep pressing until you get tired.</p>
<p>Place something with some weight to it on top of the cabbage to keep pressing while you rest.</p>
<p>Keep pressing and resting as needed, over the next hour or two. Your goal is to have the liquid rise to cover the cabbage completely. Be sure to release any air pockets that might develop.</p>
<p>If after several hours, you can’t get the liquid high enough, you can add just enough water to cover by 1 inch. Use filtered, unchlorinated water (distilled water is good). Add about ½ teaspoon of salt to each cup of water to keep the salt balance.</p>
<p>Place a weight on the cabbage to keep it from floating to the surface. Anything that floats may be exposed to air and spoil instead of ferment.</p>
<p>Cover with a fermentation tap or other device that will allow air to escape, but that does not allow air in.</p>
<p>Feel free to taste every day and decide when the sauerkraut seems best to you. Place it in the refrigerator at that point to stop the fermentation. Usually the sauerkraut is ready in 7 to 14 days, depending on your taste, room temperature and other factors. Some people believe it will have the greatest health benefits if you wait 6 to 8 weeks! I find that 10 to 14 days usually matches both my taste buds and my patience.</p>
<p>If some pieces of sauerkraut float to the top during the fermentation process, just discard them. Of course, that doesn’t matter after you refrigerate it.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>3</td><td>lbs.</td><td>cabbage</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>juniper berries, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>caraway seed, optional</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Sauerkraut</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>24</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>fermentationrecipes.com</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I usually halve this recipe unless I plan to give away at least half of the product. I like sauerkraut. It’s a great probiotic and low calorie; it’s good for you. But I just can’t eat that much sauerkraut alone.</p>
<p>Also know that I will never use the optional ingredients: I hate caraway and I think juniper berries should be reserved for their proper use in gin.</p>
<p>Finally, you must have a fermentation rig of some sort to make sauerkraut, kimchi and other types of pickles. Masontops Pickle Pipes are great silicon airlocks that work with standard Mason jars, but there are lots of options. Jessica and I have spares if you would like to try them. (And ask her about the fresh sour pickles that she makes with David.)</p>
<p>Your goal is to provide an anaerobic environment for the sauerkraut to ferment and develop.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>2 quarts</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SeansDailyMilkandHoneyBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine ¼ teaspoon of sugar and the yeast in ¼ cup warm milk. Let stand 5 to 10 minutes, until the yeast begins to foam.</p>
<p>Thoroughly mix wet ingredients in a large bowl: milk, honey, butter, and salt. Stir in yeast mixture. Stir in flour, adding a bit more if necessary to make a smooth dough. Turn dough out onto a floured surface and let rest for 5 minutes.</p>
<p>While dough is resting, clean and butter the bowl. Knead dough in the stand mixer for 7 minutes, adding flour if necessary, until the dough is smooth and silky.</p>
<p>Return dough to bowl, cover with plastic wrap, and let rise in a warm place until doubled in size. Grease loaf pan. Punch down dough. Shape dough into a loaf and put into pan. Let dough rise until doubled in size.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°F during last 20 minutes of rising. Bake for 20 to 22 minutes or until crusty and brown on top. The bread should be 190°F at the center.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ShrimpandGrits</TEXT>
categories : [ "seafood" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Prep: peel and devein shrimp. Reserve shells.</p>
<p>Grits: Melt 1 tablespoon butter in medium saucepan over medium heat. Add grits and cook, stirring often, until fragrant, about 3 minutes. Add milk, water and 3/4 teaspoon salt.</p>
<p>Increase heat to medium-high and bring to boil. Reduce heat to low. Cover and simmer, whisking often, until soft and creamy, about 25 minutes.</p>
<p>Remove from heat. Stir in remaining 2 tablespoons butter and season with salt and pepper to taste. Cover and keep warm.</p>
<p>Shrimp: While grits cook, melt 1 tablespoon butter in a 12-inch nonstick skillet over medium heat. Add shrimp shells and cook, stirring occasionally, until shells are spotty brown, about 7 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir in tomato paste and cook for 30 seconds. Add water and bring to boil, then reduce heat to low. Cover and simmer for 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Strain shrimp stock using a fine-mesh strainer, pressing to release as much liquid as possible. Discard solids. Add water if needed to make 1½ cups. Wipe skillet with paper towels.</p>
<p>Cook bacon in skillet over medium-low heat until crisp, 7-9 minutes. Increase heat to medium-high. Stir in shrimp, garlic, ½ teaspoon salt and ½ teaspoon pepper. Cook until edges of shrimp start to color, but shrimp are not cooked through. Transfer to bowl.</p>
<p>Melt 1 tablespoon butter in the skillet over medium-high heat. Whisk in flour and cook for 1 minute. Slowly whisk in shrimp stock. Bring to boil, then reduce heat to medium-low and simmer until slightly thickened, about 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir in shrimp mixture. Cover and cook until shrimp are cooked through, about 3 minutes. Remove from heat. Stir in lemon juice, Tabasco and remaining butter. Season with additional salt and pepper as needed.</p><p>Serve shrimp over grits, sprinkling with green onions. Pass extra Tabasco.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ShrimpDiane</TEXT>
categories : [ "seafood", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Rinse and peel shrimp; refrigerate. Save shells (and heads, if available).</p>
<p>Make shrimp stock, or make a faux stock: place shells in a small saucepan and cover with 1 to 2 cups of choice stock.  Bring to boil and simmer as long as possible while preparing this dish.</p>
<p>In a large skillet, melt 1 stick (½ cup) butter over high heat. When almost melted, add green onion, salt, garlic, cayenne, peppers, basil, thyme, and oregano; stir well.</p>
<p>Add mushrooms and ¼ cup shrimp stock. Shake (do not stir) the pan for about 2 to 3 minutes, until mushrooms are mostly done.</p>
<p>Add shrimp and sauté just until starting to turn pink, about 30 seconds, shaking the pan. Add the remaining ¼ cup butter, cut in chunks. Before butter melts completely, add parsley and 2 tablespoons. shrimp stock.</p>
<p>Continue cooking and shaking until the sauce is the consistency of cream.  Serve immediately.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>lb.</td><td>fresh shrimp</td></tr> <tr><td>6</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>shrimp stock</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>unsalted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>green onions, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>garlic, minced</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cayenne pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>white pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>black pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dried basil</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dried thyme</td></tr> <tr><td>1/8</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dried oregano</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>lb.</td><td>mushroom, sliced ¼-inch thick</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>fresh parsley, chopped</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "Shrimp" ]
title : <TEXT>Shrimp Diane</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Do not double this recipe. If you want to serve 4, do it twice.</p>
<p>You don't have to get shrimp with their heads; just get regular shrimp in their shells. For this recipe, you want medium-large shrimp that will cook quickly, but not get tough.</p>
<p>This can be spicy; if your cayenne pepper is particularly hot, you might cut it back a little. Paul would like you to use a full-bodied shrimp stock; that is not really necessary. In the recipe directions, it tells you how to “shrimp up” your chicken stock - this is what we usually do. Use a low-fat, low-sodium stock.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>2</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Paul Prudhomme's Louisiana Kitchen</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>We consider this to be "company food”. Since you can only make 2 servings at once, save this recipe for a more intimate dinner. Serve with rice or a good crusty French bread to soak up the sauce.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 350°F. Line a rimmed baking sheet with parchment paper.</p>
<p>Coarsely chop the bacon and cook it in a medium skillet until crisp and brown. Transfer to paper towels and drain. Drain the fat from the skillet.</p>
<p>Add oil to the skillet and sauté the onion over medium heat for about 5 minutes, until translucent.</p>

tags : [ "Rice" ]
title : <TEXT>Spanish Rice</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Steve Guinn</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is Steve's recipe, so it should probably be called Tex-Mex Rice. Unlike many Spanish Rice recipes, this one is not soggy or full of tomatoes.</p>
<p>Use ⅓ of a can of tomato paste. I don't know what you are going to do with the leftover ⅔ can of tomato paste, but don't put it in the rice. These days you can buy tubes of tomato paste; maybe that would work better.</p>
<p>Steve always fixes this rice when he cooks fajitas. It was the first thing he ever cooked for me (I guess I was impressed).</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SpicedPearGravyforFowl</TEXT>
categories : [ "thanksgiving" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Combine sugar and pears in a medium pot, stirring until sugar is dissolved. Cook over high heat for 1 minutes, stirring once or twice. Stir in 1 cup water and continue cooking until the mixture caramelizes (turns dark brown and very syrupy), about 25 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir occasionally, scraping bottom well. Remove from heat and stir in 1 cup water.  Set aside.</p>
<p>Place butter in a 10-inch skillet. Add onion, celery, bell pepper, and seasonings; sauté over high heat until vegetables are tender, about 3 minutes, stirring occasionally.</p>
<p>Add vegetable mixture and stock to the caramelized pears. Cook 15 minutes, stirring occasionally. Remove from heat.</p>
<p>Use an immersion blender and carefully puree the sauce until mostly smooth. Return to high heat and cook 2 minutes, stirring frequently.</p>
<p>Add the sliced pear; reduce heat and simmer for 5 to 7 minutes until cooked. Serve hot.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>cups</td><td>pears, peeled and chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>unsalted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>onion, finely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>celery, finely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>green bell pepper, finely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>white pepper</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>cayenne</td></tr> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>chicken stock, hot</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td></td><td>pear, peeled and sliced</td></tr></table></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SplitPeaSoup</TEXT>
categories : [ "soups", "beansandpeas" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Cut the ham steak in 4 pieces and set side.</p>
<p>Heat butter in Dutch oven over medium-high heat. Add onion and ½ teaspoon salt and cook, stirring frequently, until the onion is softened, about 3 to 4 minutes. Add the garlic and cook until fragrant, about 30 seconds. Add the water, ham steak, bacon, split peas, thyme, and bay leaves.</p>
<p>Increase the heat to high and bring to a simmer, stirring often to keep peas from sticking to the bottom.</p>
<p>Reduce heat to low, cover, and simmer until peas are tender but not falling apart, about 45 minutes.</p>
<p>Remove ham steak and cover with aluminum foil to prevent it from drying out. Stir in the carrots and celery; continue to simmer, covered, until the vegetables are tender and the peas are completely broken down, about 30 minutes longer.</p>
<p>Remove the thyme, the bay leaves, and the bacon slices.</p>
<p>Shred the ham into bite-sized pieces and return to the pot. Adjust seasonings if needed and serve hot.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>unsalted butter</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>onion, chopped fine</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cloves</td><td>garlic, pressed</td></tr> <tr><td>7</td><td>cups</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>lb.</td><td>ham steak, skin removed</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>slices</td><td>thick-cut bacon</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>dried split green peas, (1 pound)</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>sprigs</td><td>fresh thyme</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td></td><td>bay leaves</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>medium</td><td>carrots, cut in ½" pieces</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>rib</td><td>celery, cut in ½" pieces</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]

id : <TEXT>StrawberryShortcake</TEXT>
categories : [ "cakesandpies", "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Mix strawberries with ¼ to ½ cup sugar in a medium bowl; place in refrigerator. They are best if they macerate for few hours before serving. I often do this the night before.</p>

directions : <TEXT><p>Wash rice in several changes of water. Let rice drain in a sieve for 1 hour.</p>
<p>Put the rice in a heavy 2½ quart pot. Add water and bring to a boil over medium heat, covered. When steam begins to escape, turn heat to very low and cook for 20 minutes.</p>
<p>Turn heat to high for 3 seconds, then turn off. Let the pot sit undisturbed for 15 minutes -- do not lift the lid.</p>
<p>Empty rice onto a large platter or tray. In a small cup, mix together the remaining ingredients; pour over rice on tray. Fan the rice with one hand (use a magazine), while mixing with a dampened wooden spoon. Do this until rice has cooled to room temperature.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>rice, glutinous</td></tr> <tr><td>2 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>rice wine vinegar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "Rice" , "sushi"  ]
title : <TEXT>Sushi Rice</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>This makes a very sticky rice that is perfect for making sushi. Use a good Japanese rice. I am not completely sure that Japanese rice is the same thing as glutinous rice. Two good brands are Botan Calrose and Tanakaya Kokuho Rose.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>World of the East</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>6 cups</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SweetandCreamyBlackEyedPeas</TEXT>
categories : [ "beansandpeas" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>The day before: soak peas in water to cover overnight. Drain peas and set aside.</p>
<p>Combine seasoning mix ingredients in a small bowl.  Set aside.</p>
<p>Preheat a heavy 5-qt. pot over high heat to 350°F, about 4 minutes. Add 2 cups of onion, all the bell pepper and celery, and 2 tablespoons of the seasoning mix. Stir and cook for 5 minutes.</p>
<p>Stir in ½ cup stock and scrape the bottom of the pot. Cook 3 minutes. Add 1 cup onion and cook for 5 minutes more.</p>
<p>Add peas, water, and the remaining seasoning mix.  Stir.</p>
<p>Cook for 35 minutes, stirring occasionally and checking for sticking.</p>
<p>Add 1 cup apple juice and cook for 15 minutes. Add a second cup of apple juice and cook for another 15 minutes. Watch carefully for sticking. Add remaining cup of apple juice and 2 cups stock; cook for 40 minutes.</p>
<p>Add remaining stock and onions; reduce heat to medium. Cook until peas are tender, many have broken, and liquid is thick reddish-brown.  This may take 30 minutes or more.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SweetPotatoBuns</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Set aside ½ cup of the unbleached flour.</p>
<p>Place all the rest of the ingredients in the bowl of your mixer. Mix until you have a soft but not sticky dough. Add as much of the last ½ cup of flour as you need to get the right texture.</p>
<p>Knead the dough for 6 minutes.</p>
<p>Place it in a greased bowl and let rise until almost doubled, about an hour. Deflate the dough gently and divide it into 6 pieces. Give each piece a light kneading and then shape into a disc about ¾ inch thick.</p>
<p>Place on a lightly greased baking sheet. You can also bake the buns on parchment paper.  Oil the tops of the buns very lightly. Cover loosely with plastic wrap. Let rise for about 30 minutes, until almost doubled While the dough is rising, preheat the oven to 375°F.</p>
<p>Bake buns for 17 to 19 minutes, until the tops are nicely browned. Remove from the oven and cool on a rack.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>dry yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>butter, softened</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>yams, (about 1 medium)</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>nonfat dry milk powder</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>whole wheat flour</td></tr> <tr><td>2 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>unbleached flour</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Sweet Potato Buns</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>By the way, I am technically using yams and not a true sweet potato for this recipe. I don't believe that I've ever seen a true sweet potato in the South.  The orange-fleshed yams were called sweet potatoes, and I think that is common practice almost everywhere in the US.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>King Arthur Flour</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>These buns will be slightly orange, but they don't taste like sweet potatoes. They are amazingly good; this will take your hamburgers to the next level! I do find that these make a relatively heavy bun. If you don't like this, slice the bun into 3 pieces horizontally (instead of just slicing it in two). Use the middle disc to make it a "double burger," or save them to make round sandwiches with later.</p>
<p>This recipe came from the King Arthur Flour website, which I highly recommend.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>SweetPotatoCasserole</TEXT>
categories : [ "thanksgiving", "vegetables" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Preheat oven to 400°F.  Wash yams and prick all over with a fork. Bake them in their skins until done, about an hour.</p>
<p>Reduce oven temperature to 350°F. Scoop baked yams out of their skins and into the potato ricer. Squish yams through the ricer and into the food processor bowl. Add eggs, melted butter, sugar, salt, pumpkin pie spice, and vanilla. Mix until smooth.</p>
<p>Grease casserole dish or oven safe bowl. Pour yam mix into the casserole dish. Bake for 30-40 minutes, until center temp is 155°F.</p>
<p>While casserole is baking, mix flour and brown sugar in a medium-sized bowl. Cream flour and sugar with cold butter. Adjust ratio of flour and sugar to butter until the mixture is crumbly. When casserole is done, remove from oven and coat with topping mix. Lightly press tree nuts into topping. Bake until nuts are lightly toasted.</p>
<p>Serve hot as side dish. Eat again as dessert.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Casserole</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>large</td><td>yams</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>large</td><td>eggs, lightly beaten</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>unsalted butter, melted</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>pumpkin pie spice, to taste</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Topping</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>flour, approximately</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>brown sugar, approximately</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>cold butter, approximately</td></tr> <tr><td>1/3</td><td>cup</td><td>pecans, crushed</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Sweet Potato Casserole</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Other notes from Sean:</p>
<p>I don't use off-the-shelf pumpkin pie spice unless I happen to have it in the cabinet, and I usually don't. I prefer about equal portions of cinnamon, fresh ground nutmeg, and ground allspice. I like a lot of spice. I tend to add more spice mix until I can smell it over the butter and the yams in the mix. It takes more than you think to get it to that level, and not everyone likes it that way.</p>
<p>You can remove the topping altogether and use marshmallows. If you do, serve immediately. Do not put the marshmallows on, slap a lid on it, and then drive an hour to your Mother's house. When you get there, you will have a clear simple syrup on top of your casserole. It's still yummy, but it looks a little gross. Put the marshmallows on when you get there and bake it until toasted.</p>
<p>All of the topping measures are approximate because it will vary greatly depending on the shape of the dish you use. Alter the recipe to fit your dish. If you aren’t sure what to do instead of pumpkin pie spice, I recommend that you start with ½ tsp. ground cinnamon, ¼ tsp. ground ginger, and 1/8 tsp. nutmeg. Add ¼ tsp. ground allspice and ¼ tsp. ground cloves if you have them, otherwise increase the other spices a bit.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Sean Austin</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Sean cooks this every year for Thanksgiving, and we love it. I think of it as sweet potato pie without the crust. Sean says "Garnet yams are not sweet potatoes. Cognitive dissonance is required." He's right, so get over it already. Sean uses a Pyrex bread dish, but you could use an 8x8 glass casserole dish if you prefer. You can also substitute other tree nuts for the pecans, although that doesn't make any sense to us Southerners. Bake the yams a day ahead to shorten the preparation time.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>TenderBiscuits</TEXT>
categories : [ "quickbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Whisk together the dry ingredients. Stir in enough heavy cream to moisten the dough thoroughly. You may need to use only 1 cup in a humid environment, and maybe even a tiny bit more than 1¼ cup if you are in a very dry climate. You want to be able to gather the dough together and squeeze it; it should hang together easily, without dry bits falling off.</p>
<p>Turn the dough onto a lightly floured work surface, and very gently pat it into an 8-inch circle about ¾-inch thick. Use a sharp 2¼" cutter to cut rounds - or do what I do: cut the dough into squares (or even wedges) with a very sharp knife. Place the dough on a lightly greased (or parchment lined) baking sheet. Brush the biscuits with the butter, if desired.</p>
<p>Place the pan in the freezer for 30 minutes.  This improves the texture and rise of the biscuits.</p>
<p>Preheat the oven to 425°Fwhile the biscuits are in the freezer. Bake the biscuits for about 20 minutes, until they are golden brown.  Remove from the oven and serve immediately.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>unbleached flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>cornstarch</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>baking powder</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ¼</td><td>cups</td><td>heavy cream</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>melted butter, optional</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Tender Biscuits</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>King Arthur Flour</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I have a reputation for making tough biscuits and pie crusts. This recipe changed that. These biscuits are very tender; the cornstarch taste comes through as a subtle flavor that reminds me of commercial baked goods. Hmm, I wonder why! If you don't want to use cornstarch, try potato flour instead. You can add a little more sugar or a little less, to taste. I never bother with the melted butter.</p>
<p>These are amazingly easy to make, but they need to sit before cooking. So start the biscuits first, and then make the rest of the meal.  This recipe does not make good biscuits for topping other dishes or for dumplings - they will tend to fall apart.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>12 biscuits</TEXT>

title : <TEXT>Thai Coconut Chicken Soup</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>Lemongrass is a very interesting herb, and there isn't really any substitute. You should be able to find it in an Asian grocery store; I grow it in my yard.  It has a lemony flavor - but don't eat it!  Like a cinnamon stick, it is there just to provide flavor; I usually cut it in 1-inch lengths, so it is easy to find and remove from the soup. You can also cook the lemongrass in the stock for about 10 minutes and then remove it, then cook the soup as directed.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>6</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Bon Appetit, October 1992</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>I am a huge fan of Thai soups, but sometimes they are too spicy for me; this soup is not. If you are sensitive to hot peppers, you can slice the jalapeños so that you can avoid them, but they do add an important flavor. This is a fairly heavy version of the soup. If you prefer it lighter, use half as much coconut milk and twice as much stock.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>ThanksgivingTurkey</TEXT>
categories : [ "thanksgiving", "favorites", "chicken" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Let the thawed turkey stand, in its wrapping, for at least 1 hour to "warm up." It will cook more evenly if it is near room temperature before you begin cooking. However, once the turkey has reached room temperature, it should be cooked immediately. (I start cooking the turkey while it is still chilly.)</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 325°F.</p>
<p>Remove giblets.  Wash the turkey with cold water. Pat it dry inside and out. Stuff turkey if desired. If you choose to bake your stuffing separately, place the chopped onion, celery, garlic and herbs inside the cavity.  Close the cavity; I use cheap turkey trussing pins and twine (you can find these in the grocery store around the holidays).</p>
<p>Make a paste of the oil, salt and paprika. Rub this mixture all over the outside of the bird, using your hands. It''s messy. You will have plenty of paste. Place the bird in an open pan or on a roasting rack, breast side up. Cover the ends of the drumsticks and wings with aluminum foil to prevent them from over-browning. Pour the water into the bottom of the pan and place in the oven.</p>
<p>Roast until the bird is half-done. Heat the wine (do not boil it) and pour over the turkey. Wrap the turkey breast tightly with foil for the last hour of cooking. See the chart for estimated times.</p>
<p>The turkey is done when: (1) the internal temperature of the bird, in the thickest part of the thigh, is 175°F;  (2) the juices of the thigh run clear when pierced with a knife; (3) the thigh moves easily in the joint. The only sure technique is the thermometer.  If you don''t have one, get a meat thermometer - it''s cheaper than the price of a turkey.</p>
<p>Also, check the temperature of the stuffing.  It should be at least 160°F.  If the turkey is done, but the stuffing is not, take the turkey out and remove the stuffing to a buttered baking dish.  Put the stuffing back in the oven while the turkey rests.</p>
<p>Let the turkey stand for 15 minutes before carving; the temperature of the thigh should rise to 180°F.  Even if the turkey is late, let it stand and be a little later.  Otherwise, it will be dry.</p>
<p>Estimated cooking times:</p>
<p>14-16 lb.  --  3 ½ to 3 ¾ hours</p>
<p>16-18 lb.  --  3 ¾ to 4 hours</p>
<p>18-20 lb.  --  4 to 4 ½ hours</p>
<p>20-22 lbs --  4 ½ to 5 hours</p>
<p>22-24 lbs -- 5 to 5 ½ hours</p>
<p>The cooking time can vary even more than 30 minutes based on individual oven differences and the temperature of the turkey when you began cooking it.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>4</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>vegetable oil</td></tr> <tr><td>4</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>paprika</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>white wine</td></tr> <tr><td>20</td><td>lbs.</td><td>turkey</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>For the cavity (if not stuffing the bird)</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>medium</td><td>onion, coarsely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>ribs</td><td>celery, coarsely chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>6</td><td>cloves</td><td>garlic, peeled (as many or f</td></tr> <tr><td>6</td><td>sprigs</td><td>fresh herbs, sage, parsley, thyme as desired</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "turkey" ]
title : <TEXT>Thanksgiving Turkey</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>A lot of "fresh, never frozen" turkeys have hard, icy giblets, because they are chilled to 26°F. Get a fresh bird at least 24 hours before you intend to cook it, so you will have plenty of time to thaw it properly. Turkeys are not considered frozen until they reach 24°F, and are frozen solid. Thawing a  truly frozen bird in the refrigerator will take about 24 hours for every 5 pounds, so a 20 pound frozen turkey will take 4 days.  If you thaw a frozen bird in cold water, changing the water frequently, it will only take 30 minutes per pound (still, that would be about 10 hours for the 20 lb. frozen bird).</p>
<p>As you are planning your holiday meal and deciding when to start the turkey, give yourself about 30 minutes to wrestle with stuffing the turkey and getting it in the oven. It's never as quick and easy as I think it's going to be.</p>
<p>You should plan for about 1½ pounds of turkey per person; this will give you plenty of left-overs, unless you buy a really small bird.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Diestel Turkey Farm & Lisa Guinn</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Since I only cook turkey once or twice a year, I am hardly an expert. However, I have had consistently good results with this recipe. By the way, you can baste the turkey if you want, but it doesn't help it cook and it doesn't make the meat more moist. Some people think that salting the outside of the bird will dry it out; you can leave the salt out of this recipe if you like. I'm not sure it makes any difference.In my experience, the most important factor is that the turkey is completely thawed. A properly thawed turkey will cook more evenly and will not dry out as much before it is done. It will also get done close to the time you expect, not 2 hours later!</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Dissolve yeast in 1 cup water in a small bowl. If you use the egg, place it in a measuring cup with the second cup of water, so that the combination of egg and water equals one cup; add this to the yeast.</p>
<p>Sift flour with sugar and salt into a large bowl. Add herbs to flour and stir to mix. Add the water to the flour and stir well to make a soft, sticky dough.</p>
<p>Beat vigorously with a wooden spoon for several minutes. Cover the bowl with a towel and let rise until double, about 1 hour.</p>
<p>Punch dough down by stirring with a spoon; divide into 2 parts, placing each into well-greased pans. Cover and let rise again until double.</p>

id : <TEXT>TheVeryBestSteakEver</TEXT>
categories : [ "beef", "favorites" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Remove steak from refrigerator. Pat dry and place on a rack for at least 15 minutes and up to 30 minutes. Lightly oil meat - as lightly as possible on both sides. Pat with paper towels to remove excess oil if necessary. Generously salt and pepper both sides on meat. Really rub the salt into the meat. Let meat rest on the rack for 5 minutes or more. It is best for the steak to come to room temperature for greatest control of the cooking.</p>
<p>Place a cast iron skillet over the highest heat for 3 minutes. Turn on exhaust vent (or open windows). Carefully lower a steak into the pan -- once it touches the pan, DO NOT SLIDE IT OR MOVE IT. (So if you are planning to cook a second steak in the same pan at the same time, be very careful about your placement.) Do NOT touch the meat for 2 ½ minutes.  Leave the heat on high. Carefully turn steak over and cook the second side for 2 minutes. Move the meat to a clean rack. Cover loosely with foil or an inverted bowl. Let stand for 5 minutes. DO NOT SKIP THIS STEP.  (Not even for the last steak. How would you like to have to wait for the last steak and then find that yours was tougher and drier than everyone else''s? That would be doubly bad.)</p>
<p>The time given is for a rib-eye, about ½ to ¾ inch thick, cooked to medium. If your stove is hotter than mine, the meat thicker, or you like your meat more rare, then you will need to adjust your time appropriately.  Whatever you do - don''t be afraid to push the limits a little bit and DON''T MOVE THE MEAT. Pick a time and live with it.  Adjust future steaks based on experience.</p>
<p>Steve’s alternative: Preheat the oven to 400°F. Using the above technique, sear the steak on each side until browned, then place in oven for about 5 minutes. If you want to remove the steak from the skillet into the oven, then make sure you have a preheated pan in the oven for the steak.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>8</td><td>ounces</td><td>steak</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "Grilled", "steak" ]
title : <TEXT>The Very Best Steak Ever</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>1</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Alton Brown, I'm Just Here for the Food</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>It doesn't really matter what the weight of the steak is, or what kind of steak it is. I think this is a great way to cook rib-eye. The key concern is the size (it needs to fit in a pan) and the thickness (which affects cooking time). This truly is the greatest steak I've ever cooked, thanks to Alton Brown. The first time I cooked this, I even overcooked the steak a little (it was no longer pink in the middle) - and it was still better than any steak I'd ever had in a restaurant or just about anywhere. Unbelievable, and so easy.</p>
<p>You can make as many steaks as you like, but you are obviously limited by the number of appropriate pans and stove burners.  It is possible to cook 2 steaks in the same pan at the same time - if the steaks are small and you are very careful. It is also best to do multiple steaks on a gas range, as it gets much hotter than an electric range. Electric just doesn't put out enough heat to sear more than one steak at a time very effectively.</p>
<p>Be aware that this technique will create smoke in your kitchen, especially for steaks with more fat. Open windows, use a fan, turn off the smoke detectors.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>VegetarianChili</TEXT>
categories : [ "beansandpeas", "soups" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Simmer the lentils in water for 40 to 45 minutes, until tender. Drain the lentils, reserving the liquid.</p>
<p>Heat oil in a large saucepan. Sauté onion and bell pepper for 10 minutes. Add garlic and sauté for 1 to 2 minutes. Add tomatoes. Add drained beans and lentils to the saucepan. Add paprika and chili powder.</p>
<p>Simmer 15 minutes, adding water from lentils as needed to keep the appropriate consistency. Season with salt and pepper, and add a pinch of sugar. Garnish and serve.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>olive oil</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>medium</td><td>onion, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td></td><td>red bell pepper, chopped</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cloves</td><td>garlic, crushed</td></tr> <tr><td>14</td><td>ounces</td><td>canned tomatoes</td></tr> <tr><td>30</td><td>ounces</td><td>canned kidney beans, drained</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>lentils</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>paprika</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>chili powder, Gebhart's</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td>pinch</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>chopped fresh cilantro, for garnish</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [ "Beans" ]
title : <TEXT>Vegetarian Chili</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You may use 1 cup dried kidney beans, cooked and drained, instead of the two 15-oz cans. French green lentils, instead of the common brown lentils, will have a much better texture and flavor for this dish.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>4</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>The Complete Vegetarian Cuisine</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is a good chili recipe.  I served it at Jessica's 4H club horse show (several of the kids were vegetarian), and lots of people ate it, even though there was also regular chili available.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>WalnutBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Heat oil in a heavy large skillet over medium heat. Add onion and sauté until tender, about 5 minutes. Remove from heat and let cool.</p>
<p>Combine water and honey in a large bowl. Sprinkle with yeast and stir to blend. Let stand until foamy, about 10 minutes. Mix in onions, salt, and ½ cup bread flour.</p>
<p>In a separate bowl, blend the whole wheat flour and the dry milk. Add this blend to the dough, 1 cup at a time. Cover the dough and let it stand for 5 minutes to hydrate. Blend in enough of the remaining 2 cups of bread flour to form a smooth ball.  Transfer to a floured work surface and knead until smooth and elastic, about 3 minutes. If the dough is too sticky to knead, oil your hands and use a stretching/folding technique instead of kneading. Lightly oil a large bowl. Place dough in bowl and turn to coat surface. Cover and let rise until double, about 45 minutes.</p>
<p>Grease a heavy large baking sheet, or two loaf pans. Punch dough down and turn out onto a floured work surface. Sprinkle with walnuts; knead to incorporate. Divide dough in half.</p>
<p>Place in greased loaf pans; or, form into round loaves and place on baking sheet.</p>
<p>Cover and let rise until almost doubled, about 45 minutes. Preheat oven to 400°F.</p>
<p>Bake loaves until well-browned, about 25 minutes. Loaves should sound hollow when tapped on the bottom. Transfer to racks; cool.</p></TEXT>

id : <TEXT>WaterRisenFrenchBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>All the water in this recipe should be between 120 and 130°F - as hot as it comes out of the faucet, more or less.</p>
<p>Mix flours, yeast, and salt in a medium bowl. Add oil and then all of the water. Stir until the bowl is clean and all the flour has been picked up. Fill a large bowl with hot water. Drop the dough into the bowl of hot water. The dough will sink, but will float in 10 minutes.</p>
<p>After 10 minutes, remove dough immediately to a work surface that has been dusted with ¼ flour; sprinkle remaining ¼ cup flour on top.  (Dry your hands now.)</p>
<p>Knead gently for about 5 minutes, adding more flour only if needed to keep dough from sticking. Divide dough in thirds. Knead each piece for 1 minute, then roll out and shape into a 12-inch long loaf. Place on greased cookie sheet or in French bread pans, if you have them. Leave as much room as possible between loaves. (You can even use a baking stone.)</p>
<p>Place dough in cold oven and spray with a fine mist of water. Turn oven on its lowest setting for exactly 1 minute, then turn off. Let dough rest in the oven for 15 minutes, then remove dough.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 400°F for 10 minutes. Place dough (which should have doubled) in the oven and mist again with water. After 15 minutes, open the oven and mist the dough yet again. Bread should be done in 5 to 9 minutes more. Cool on racks for 10 minutes before cutting.</p>
<p>To reheat: place in a 400°F oven and spray with water. Heat for 4 minutes.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>bread flour</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>flour, unbleached</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>pkg</td><td>yeast, quick-acting or Rapid-Rise</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>oil</td></tr> <tr><td>1 1/3</td><td>cups</td><td>hot water</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>flour, unbleached</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Water-Risen French Bread</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>12</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Arkansas Gazette</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>Trust me on the water thing here. It works and it's fast. This is the bread that I make when we want to have bread for dinner, and dinner is already getting started!</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>three 12-inch loaves</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>WholeWheatBread</TEXT>
categories : [ "yeastbreads" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>The day before, make the soaker and the poolish. For the soaker: Mix the soaker ingredients in a bowl. Cover with plastic wrap and leave at room temperature until the next day. For the poolish: Mix together the flour and yeast, then stir in the water to make a thick paste. Stir only until the flour is hydrated. Cover the bowl with plastic wrap and let ferment for 2 to 4 hours, or until it just begins to bubble. Then place it in the refrigerator overnight.</p>
<p>To complete the bread: One hour before you begin, remove the poolish from the refrigerator. In a mixing bowl, stir together the flour, salt and yeast. Then add the poolish and the soaker, as well as the honey, oil and egg. Stir with a large metal spoon (or mix on low speed for about 1 minute with the paddle attachment) until the dough forms a ball. Add more water or flour if needed. Transfer dough to a floured work surface. Knead until the dough forms a firm, supple dough. This will take 10 to 15 minutes by hand, slightly less by machine. The dough will be tacky, not sticky.  It should pass the windowpane test. Lightly oil a large bowl. Add the dough and turn to coat. Cover with plastic wrap. Let rise until double, about 2 hours.</p>
<p>Divide the dough into 2 equal pieces. Shape into loaves. Mist the tops with oil and cover loosely with plastic wrap. Proof at room temperature for about 90 minutes, or until the dough nearly doubles in size and is cresting over the lip of the pans.</p>
<p>Preheat oven to 350°F. Bake the loaves for 30 minutes, then rotate for even baking. Continue baking for 15 to 30 minutes longer. The finished bread should register between 185 and 190°F.  It should sound hollow when thumped on the bottom. If the loaves are soft and squishy on the sides, return them to the pans and continue baking until done. Allow loaves to cool for at least 1 hour before slicing or serving.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Soaker</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>whole wheat flour, or other coarse flour</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>water, at room temp</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Poolish</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>cups</td><td>whole wheat flour, (6¾ oz)</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dry yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>water, at room temp</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Dough</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>cups</td><td>whole wheat flour, (9 oz)</td></tr> <tr><td>1 1/3</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>dry yeast</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>honey</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>dry milk</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>vegetable oil, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>large</td><td>egg, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>Tablespoon</td><td>gluten, wheat, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>diastatic malt, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>1/8</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>ascorbic acid, optional</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td>Tablespoons</td><td>sesame seeds, optional garnish</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Whole Wheat Bread</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>24</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Modified from The Bread Bakers Apprentice</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This makes an excellent 100% whole wheat bread. It is not as light as white bread, but it is close. It does not have a very yeasty taste; the flavor is mild and the crumb is fine. The wheat gluten, diastatic malt and ascorbic acid are completely optional, but they will help the bread rise at least 10% higher. Since I bake bread almost every week, I think it's worth it.  </p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT>2 loaves</TEXT>

id : <TEXT>WolfgangsCheesecake</TEXT>
categories : [ "desserts" ]
directions : <TEXT><p>Crust: Grease and flour a 9-inch (or 10-inch) spring form pan. Separate the bottom and the sides of the pan. Preheat the oven to 400°F.</p>
<p>In a large bowl, use a hand mixer to beat the butter and sugar until fluffy. Beat in the egg yolk, lemon peel and vanilla. Add flour and combine well, but beat slowly and only until well-mixed. With well-floured hands, press 1/3 of the dough onto the bottom of the pan. Place the dough in the center and use the palm of your hand to push it to the edges of the pan bottom. Bake the bottom crust for 8 to 10 minutes, until the crust is lightly browned. Let the bottom crust cool, then attach the sides of the pan to the bottom. With well-floured hands, spread the remaining dough over the sides of the pan. Carefully join the dough to the crust at the bottom of the pan. If this is all you accomplish for the day, put the crust in the refrigerator until you complete the filling.</p>
<p>Filling: Preheat oven to 500°F. Slice cream cheese into a large bowl. With a hand mixer, combine cream cheese, sugar, flour, orange rind, lemon peel and vanilla. Beat until smooth and well blended. (The rinds tend to clump around the beaters.) Add eggs and egg yolks, one at a time; blend into the mixture. Mix in the heavy cream. Pour the mixture into the prepared crust. Place a piece of aluminum foil under the pan, in case the pan leaks. Bake at 500°Ffor 8 minutes. Reduce heat and bake at 250°Ffor 70 minutes.</p>
<p>Since it is often difficult to determine when the cheesecake is done, test it with a toothpick in the center - when the toothpick comes out clean (mixture-free), the cheesecake is usually done. Cool the cheesecake in the pan. After a couple of hours, you can put it in the refrigerator. When cool, invert the pan on a large plate covered with parchment paper. Remove the pan carefully, especially the bottom. Use a spatula if necessary to detach the crust from the pan. Invert the cheesecake (to put it back right-side up) on a serving dish or plate.</p>
<p>Topping: Rinse and drain the raspberries and blueberries. Crush enough of the "defective" berries to make 1 cup. Combine the crushed berries, sugar, water, cornstarch and salt in a saucepan. Cook the mixture, stirring most of the time with a wooden spoon, until it is clear and thick. Cook 2 minutes more; the mixture will begin to boil. Remove from heat; add butter. Strain the mixture through a sieve and allow to cool. Artfully arrange the remaining berries on the cheesecake. Cover the cheesecake, top and sides, with the cooled glaze.</p>
<p>Chill the cheesecake in the refrigerator for at least 4 hours, though longer is better. (It seems the best one day after cutting out the first 1 or 2 pieces.)</p>
<p>Cooking notes from past experience:</p>
<p>- if the bottom crust is thin, you may need to stop cooking at 8 minutes instead of 9.</p>
<p>- the filling did not rise to the last inch of my 10-inch pan, so the last inch of side crust was over-browned.  The crust was spread too thin overall, because my pan is a bit tall for the recipe.</p>
<p>- I baked it for an extra 20 minutes, but it still failed the toothpick test.  And yet, it seemed overdone.</p></TEXT>
ingredients : <TEXT><table id="ingredients-table"> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Crust</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>cup</td><td>butter, at room temperature</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td></td><td>egg yolk</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>grated lemon peel</td></tr> <tr><td>1/2</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>cup</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Filling</td></tr> <tr><td>40</td><td>ounces</td><td>cream cheese, at room temperature</td></tr> <tr><td>1 3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>3</td><td>tablespoons</td><td>flour</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>grated orange peel</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>teaspoons</td><td>grated lemon peel</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>vanilla extract</td></tr> <tr><td>5</td><td>large</td><td>eggs</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td></td><td>egg yolks</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>heavy cream</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td></td><td>Topping</td></tr> <tr><td>16</td><td>ounces</td><td>raspberries, or more</td></tr> <tr><td>16</td><td>ounces</td><td>blueberries, or more</td></tr> <tr><td>3/4</td><td>cups</td><td>sugar</td></tr> <tr><td>1/4</td><td>cup</td><td>water</td></tr> <tr><td>1 ½</td><td>tablespoons</td><td>cornstarch</td></tr> <tr><td></td><td>dash</td><td>salt</td></tr> <tr><td>1</td><td>teaspoon</td><td>butter</td></tr></table></TEXT>
tags : [  ]
title : <TEXT>Wolfgang's Cheesecake</TEXT>
notes : <TEXT><div id="notes"><p>You can use frozen or fresh berries for the topping. If you use frozen, thaw and drain them; add any drained juice to the glaze.</p>
<p>I have learned that you can't trust the toothpick test when a large cheesecake is still in the oven. Carry-over will continue to cook it for quite some time,
so you need to remove it from the oven while it is still a little soft in the middle, especially if the outside few inches are done.</p>
</div></TEXT>
servings : <TEXT>24</TEXT>
source : <TEXT>Wolfgang Demmel</TEXT>
time : <TEXT></TEXT>
introduction : <TEXT><p>This is Wolfgang's famous cheesecake, and rightly so. You can top it with whatever you like, but I have entered only the raspberry/blueberry topping, because I like it the best. Wolfgang does not advise pineapple topping.</p>
<p>This is a huge cheesecake, very rich. You should not eat more than a very small slice at one sitting. I'd guess that it could easily serve 2 dozen people.</p></TEXT>
yield : <TEXT></TEXT>
